*Note: This entry is placed under Rivals/Enemies for historical-origin reasons; in the present taxonomy it could equally belong under Intimate Allies. The boundary is exactly the point.*

---

### 8. The Older Self / Kid Cable — the Internal Enemy as External Event

**Origin.** In *Extermination*, a younger version of the subject (the adolescent "Kid Cable") murders the adult version and replaces him. This is, in plain language, suicide-by-prior-self. The adult subject had become, in the younger one's assessment, a man who had failed his own youthful standard.

**Dynamics.** There is no other relationship in the subject's life that more nakedly externalizes the structure of his self-loathing. The young self looks at the old self and finds him insufficient. The old self does not, in the moment, fight as hard as he could. The kill is permitted.

**Trust / safety.** Not applicable in the conventional sense. The two are, ontologically, the same person at different epochs; the safety question is therefore whether the subject is safe from his own earlier conviction, and the answer is no.

**Failure mode.** The adult subject's failure mode here is *consent to replacement*. He had organized his life as a transitional instrument; the moment a viable successor (himself, younger) appeared, the instrument made itself available for retirement-by-elimination.

**Leverage.** The young self holds the old self's original idealism, unsoftened. The old self holds nothing comparable — experience does not weigh against innocence in this account. The transaction was always going to go one way.

---

## II. INTIMATE / LOVERS

A short list. The subject has been intimate with strikingly few people across a subjectively century-plus lifespan. The pattern is consistent: every intimate has been a combat operator, a precognitive, a telepath, or some combination. He has never partnered with a civilian. The selection criterion appears to be *can this person stand next to me in a firefight* before any other consideration, including attraction.

---

### 1. Domino / Neena Thurman — the Primary Adult Attachment

**Origin and history.** Met during the early Six Pack / Wild Pack mercenary period, prior to the New Mutants. The longest-running intimate relationship in the subject's life. Complicated, additionally, by the existence of Copycat (Vanessa Carlysle), who impersonated Domino during a significant portion of the subject's early relationship with "her" — meaning the subject was, for a period, intimate with a shapeshifter while believing he was with Domino, and then had to reckon with the real Domino's separate history when the substitution was revealed.

**Dynamics.** Domino is the only person the subject treats as an unambiguous *peer*. She does not require his protection (her probability-warping power makes her, in some respects, more survivable than he is), she does not look to him for instruction, and she does not require him to perform certainty. With her, the subject is closest to whatever his baseline state would be in the absence of mission. The relationship is intermittent — they separate and reunite across decades — but it is never antagonistic in the periods between, which is unusual for him.

**Trust / safety.** High in both directions, with one specific limit: the subject does not, even with Domino, share the full ledger of what virus containment costs him moment to moment. She knows; he does not narrate it. She does not require him to.

**Sexual / physical patterns.** The relationship is physical and uncomplicated by either of them, which is, again, atypical for him. There is a working theory in the subject's own internal life — never articulated aloud — that Domino is the only partner with whom he does not, on some level, feel he is contaminating her by proximity to the T-O.

**Failure mode.** The relationship cannot survive sustained co-habitation. Both parties default to mission and disappear from each other for years at a time, then resume. The failure is not infidelity or conflict; it is incapacity for the domestic register. Neither of them can do ordinary life and they have stopped pretending they should try.

**Leverage.** Domino has more leverage on the subject than anyone alive — she is the one person whose disapproval registers as a personal cost rather than a tactical one. She rarely uses it. When she does, it works.

---

### 2. Copycat / Vanessa Carlysle — the Impersonation

**Origin.** A shapeshifter who replaced Domino during the Six Pack / early Cable period, conducting a long-form intimate deception. The subject was in a sexual and emotional relationship with someone he believed was Domino, and was not.

**Dynamics in retrospect.** This is, structurally, one of the most clinically interesting events in the subject's life: a person whose entire psychology is organized around vigilance, identity, and the question *who is the real one and who is the copy* was sexually intimate with a copy for an extended period without detecting it. The parallel to the Stryfe/Cable original-or-clone question is unmistakable, and the subject has, in his more reflective moments, registered the irony.

**Trust / safety.** Annihilated on discovery. The subject does not maintain a relationship with Copycat afterward in any meaningful sense; she becomes an intelligence variable rather than a person to him.

**Failure mode.** The deeper failure is the subject's: he wanted to be with Domino badly enough that he did not interrogate the small discrepancies. Vigilance has blind spots, and intimacy is the largest of them. He has not, since, allowed himself to forget this.

**Leverage.** Copycat retains nothing operationally. The leverage is internal — the subject's permanent residual doubt about the reliability of his own intimate perception. It contributes, materially, to his lifelong difficulty with vulnerability.

---

### 3. Aliya / Jenskot — the Wife in the Future

**Origin.** Cable's wife in the far-future Askani timeline, daughter of the Clan Chieftain (in some accounts), member of the resistance, mother of Tyler. Met and married during the period after he had been raised by the Clan Askani and become an adult warrior in the Apocalypse War.

**Dynamics.** This is the only marriage of the subject's life, and it was conducted in the only period of his life where he had a clear, stable cultural surround — the Askani movement, with its rituals, prophecies, and structures. Jenskot was not a peer in the Domino sense; she was a *co-religionist*, a fellow believer in the prophecy that the subject embodied. The intimacy was theologically framed. They had a son together.

**End.** Jenskot was killed during the war, in circumstances connected to Stryfe's faction. Her death is the closest thing to an original wound in the subject's *adult* psychology, distinct from the originary infantile wounds. The Apocalypse-war losses were many; this one defines them.

**Trust / safety in life.** High. They were married in a community that took marriage seriously and operated together in combat. There is no evidence of relational dysfunction; the relationship was ended by external violence, not internal failure.

**Failure mode (in memory).** The subject does not speak of her. The absence of speech is the symptom. He has, across decades of narrative, never volunteered her name without prompting. He has not remarried. He has not sought a second long-form domestic partnership of comparable kind. The wound is sealed by silence and silence is how he protects it.

**Leverage.** None living. The memory itself is the leverage, and it is leverage only against himself.

---

### 4. Tyler / Genesis — the Lost Son (Lover entry by parental adjacency — see also Family file)

*Listed here only to mark the dynamic: the failure of the marriage-and-fatherhood project, via the loss of Jenskot and the subsequent loss of Tyler to Apocalypse's conditioning, is the single largest pre-Hope reason for the subject's adult retreat from intimacy. Tyler does not belong in this section in his own right — see family dossier — but every entry above is shaped by the fact that the subject already tried to have a family and lost it to the same forces he is still fighting.*

---

### 5. Brief and Ambiguous Intimacies

The record contains scattered indications of brief encounters during the Six Pack mercenary period and during the Soldier X wandering — a transient connection in an Eastern European town here, a partner-of-convenience in a war camp there. None develop. The pattern is consistent: brief, physical, terminated by departure rather than by conflict. The subject does not appear to seek casual intimacy actively; he accepts it when it arrives in a way that does not require him to stay.

**Trust / safety in these encounters.** Low to none, mutually understood. The subject does not deceive partners about his unavailability; he is, in this narrow domain, scrupulously honest.

**Failure mode.** None internal — the encounters are designed to fail in a controlled way. The failure is structural: a man who has lost a wife and a son to a war that has not ended cannot, while the war persists, allow another such loss. The brief encounters are the form of intimacy that respects this.

---

## III. CROSS-PATTERN OBSERVATIONS

**The shared substrate.** Every meaningful enemy in this file is a *version* of the subject (Stryfe = the clone, Apocalypse = the principle that designed him, Sinister = the man who built him, Bishop = the soldier he was before he became a parent, Kid Cable = the youth he was before he became tired, Deadpool = the body-as-battlefield twin). The subject does not have enemies in the ordinary sense. He has externalized self-states wearing other faces. This is why the war is endless: every defeat is a partial self-defeat, and every victory leaves a residue.

**The intimacy criterion.** Every intimate of meaningful duration has been a combat operator with abilities that exceed or complement his own and a temperament that does not require him to soften. He has never tested whether he could be intimate with someone outside the operational frame, because he has assumed — probably correctly, given his somatic reality — that he cannot.

**The asymmetry that he cannot close.** In every relationship in this file, the subject is either the dominant operator (Hope, X-Force, the MLF, Sinister-as-tool-of-information) or in fixed structural inferiority (Stryfe holds the originary doubt; Apocalypse holds the originary infection; the dead wife holds the only marriage; the younger self held the right to replace him). He has, with exactly two people, occupied something resembling peer position: Domino and Deadpool. Both relationships are characterized by intermittency, by the refusal of domestic continuity, and by combat as the medium of contact. This is the closest he gets and it is, by ordinary measures, not very close.

**Operative summary.** The subject's antagonistic and intimate fields are continuous rather than opposed. The same selection pressures — vigilance, mission-compatibility, somatic understanding, the long view — produce both his enemies and his lovers. He is, in this domain, exactly as efficient and exactly as lonely as the rest of his life predicts.


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Preface: The Starving Giant

Every accurate sentence about Nathan Summers' capabilities must begin with a ratio. He is, genetically, one of the most powerful psionics ever conceived — the optimized product of the two most potent telepathic and telekinetic lineages in the recorded mutant gene pool (Grey via Pryor; Summers as the structural lattice). Conservative readings of his unimpeded potential place him in the Omega bracket on both axes; the Askani texts treat him, with cause, as a once-per-millennium event. In practice, the *expressed* power is a thin pilot light atop a furnace permanently rented out to an autoimmune war. Anywhere between 90% and 98% of his psionic bandwidth is conscripted, every waking and sleeping moment, to suppressing the techno-organic virus colonizing his body from the left shoulder outward. What the world sees — what enemies fight, what allies rely on — is the *overflow*. The signature is therefore not the power but the *budget*: every action is a withdrawal from a balance that, if drawn down too far, kills him from the inside in hours.

This is the master frame. Treat every ability below as both a capacity and a cost.

---

## 1. Telekinesis

**Mechanism.** Direct cortical manipulation of matter and force at a distance, expressed through visible blue-white psionic discharge when at intensity, invisible at low load. Operates from the macro scale (lifting vehicles, deflecting ballistic and energy weapons) down to the cellular and sub-cellular (the function that holds the T-O virus in check is technically a sustained, hyper-fine telekinetic operation against his own tissue, individually inhibiting nano-scale conversion vectors).

**Range.** Demonstrated effective combat range: line-of-sight, optimal at 10–30 meters, degrades with distance and obstruction. Demonstrated extreme: orbital and trans-orbital feats during peak unbinding episodes (Providence-era; *Cable* vol. 2 peaks; the brief unrestricted intervals where the virus is in remission or externally suppressed).

**Granular applications, in observed frequency order:**
- **Ballistic deflection.** A constant low-intensity field around his torso and head; he does not "raise shields," he runs them. This is why bullets aimed at him often appear to *miss*; many do not — they are nudged.
- **Recoil cancellation and weapon stabilization.** His signature heavy ordnance is fired one-handed at calibers that should not be fired one-handed. The TK absorbs the recoil and corrects the muzzle climb. This is also why his accuracy with grossly oversized weapons is anomalous: the round is mid-flight-steered within a few degrees of arc.
- **Self-locomotion.** Short-range augmented leaps, controlled falls, "TK-assisted" running. He almost never flies overtly — flight burns budget — but he is constantly cheating gravity by single-digit percentages.
- **Fine manipulation.** Field strip and reassembly of a weapon mid-fall, hot-wire of an unfamiliar vehicle without touching it, the disarming of an opponent by removing the firing pin remotely.
- **Macro feats (rare, expensive).** Lifting structures, stopping vehicles, redirecting artillery. These leave him grey-faced, sweating, and noticeably weaker for hours afterward — and they almost always coincide with a measurable advance of the virus in the following day.

**Limits.** Hard ceiling imposed by viral overhead. Fine control is preserved; gross strength is rationed. He cannot sustain "shield wall" defense for an entire team for long. He will preferentially expend on others' children before himself.

---

## 2. Telepathy

**Mechanism.** Full-spectrum mind-to-mind: passive ambient reception (which he keeps shuttered nearly all the time — see below), active scan, broadcast, mind-link, memory retrieval, illusion-casting, psychic combat on the astral plane.

**Why it appears weak.** It is not weak; it is *triaged*. Telepathy is metabolically the more expensive of the two psionic systems for him, because it has to be conducted through the same cortical structures the T-O virus is most aggressively colonizing — every scan is a stress test on the front line of the infection. He keeps it dark by default. When he uses it, three patterns recur:

- **Surgical, brief, narrow-aperture.** A single thought lifted from a single mind; a one-sentence broadcast to a teammate; a name confirmed. Never a sweep of a room when a glance will do.
- **The Askani link.** A specialized, lower-cost channel inherited from his training, used to communicate with Rachel, with Hope at distance, and historically with the Clan. Operates closer to spiritual practice than to raw telepathy and seems to draw on a different reservoir.
- **Combat psi-shock.** A focused stun-strike delivered in close quarters, generally to a single target, generally to end a fight rather than to extract intelligence.

**Limits and refusals.** He will not deep-scan allies and visibly hates being asked to. This is partly ethics (a Xavier inheritance he kept) and partly self-protection: every involuntary telepath knows that the deeper you go into another mind the more of yours they take with them, and Nathan cannot afford to give any of his away. The *refusal* is a power signature in itself.

---

## 3. The Techno-Organic Virus as a Capability

A counterintuitive but necessary entry. The T-O infection is primarily a disease. It is also, in narrow circumstances, an *instrument*.

- **Interface.** He can directly mind-meld with machinery through the converted tissue — read code by touch, slave drones, talk to satellites without a console. He uses this sparingly because every such interface is an invitation to the virus to escalate; the discipline boundary is the same membrane the disease is trying to cross.
- **Structural hardness.** The converted regions of his left arm and torso are, simply, harder than flesh. He has taken blade and small-arms hits to that quadrant that should have ended him and walked away with cosmetic damage.
- **Self-repair (limited).** Necrotic tissue in the conversion zone reconstitutes itself, slowly, between fights — but always more *converted* than before. Each "healing" is a small surrender.

The capability and the kill condition are the same substance. This is not metaphor; it is mechanism.

---

## 4. Tactical, Strategic, and Operational Skills

These are not powers; they are the accumulated craft of subjective decades of war, and in many engagements they matter more than the psionics.

- **Small-unit command.** Trained by the resistance cells of the Askani war, refined through New Mutants/X-Force/X-Force-Krakoa. Reads a room of operators in seconds, assigns by capability with near-perfect economy, communicates in clipped phrases pre-tested for ambiguity. Notable habit: he will repeat a call sign once and only once; the second non-response is treated as a casualty event.
- **Long-horizon strategy.** Operates on planning cycles measured in years and, where the time-travel capability is online, in centuries. Maintains contingency trees of branching futures, updated in his head, against which present events are evaluated for trajectory. The Providence project was a 25-year plan executed openly while concealing its second-order objectives.
- **Counter-intelligence and information discipline.** Compulsive compartmentalization. Teammates routinely discover, post-hoc, that he was running a parallel operation they were not briefed on. He does not enjoy doing this; he believes the alternative is worse.
- **Marksmanship.** Elite under any baseline. With TK augmentation, functionally inerrant within effective range. He prefers heavy precision rifles and his signature plasma/projectile longarm; he can run almost any small arm from any era of Earth and several non-Earth platforms.
- **Close-quarters and blade.** Competent rather than artistic — he treats melee as a failure mode of his preferred standoff and will end it as fast as possible, typically with a single disabling strike augmented by a TK nudge.
- **Languages.** Native English; functional in Russian (Soldier X period), Japanese, several future-dialects no one else speaks; reading-only in a half-dozen more. Communicates with Askani-derived constructs through a partly-glossolalic ritual register that he uses with Rachel and used with Hope.
- **Field medicine.** Self-taught and brutal — he can stabilize a sucking chest wound, set a femur, run an IV blind. On himself, has performed minor field surgery (round extraction, debridement of T-O conversion margins) without anesthesia.
- **Vehicle and weapons mechanic.** Will fix what he is given. Can build crude firearms and explosives from scratch; can fly anything with a stick; reads code natively due to the T-O interface.

---

## 5. Time Travel (the Bodyslide)

**Mechanism.** Personal teleportation through both space and time, via the "bodyslide" — originally executed using harnessed devices, later partially internalized; in his prime, performable solo on willpower and a code phrase ("bodyslide by one," "by two," etc.). The mechanism is part technological (future-era apparatus and implants) and part psionic.

**Costs.** Catastrophic. A solo slide leaves him debilitated. Group slides have on multiple occasions cost him weeks of recovery and accelerated the virus visibly. Multi-millennium jumps with a passenger (the long voyage with Hope) consumed the technology, the body, and ultimately the life. He treats the bodyslide the way a 20th-century state treats nuclear weapons: present in every calculation, used only when nothing else will suffice.

**Limits and constraints.**
- Cannot freely re-enter eras he has already heavily modified without paradox cost.
- Cannot reliably bring back the dead by jumping to before they died — a discipline he has tested and abandoned. The branching he creates is not the timeline he left.
- Each jump frays his ability to perceive his own native present as singular; he experiences "now" as a thin slice of a continuum, which is part of why he is so emotionally remote in real time.

---

## 6. Skill Growth Over Time

A longitudinal reading of the capability set:

- **Askani childhood (subj. ages 0–14).** Raw psionics suppressed almost entirely by viral onset and by Clan training, which favored discipline over expression. Combat instruction begins absurdly early. Marksmanship and small-unit doctrine established before puberty.
- **Resistance youth and middle age (subj. 15–~45).** The cyborg-soldier phase. Capabilities are predominantly martial and technological. Psionics treated as a private medical regimen, not an offensive tool. He himself does not yet know how powerful he is.
- **First Cable era / New Mutants & X-Force (chronologically late 80s–mid 90s).** Public capability set is "big gun, big arm, vague psi." He is concealing the psionics deliberately, partly because Stryfe could exploit them, partly because Xavier-trained colleagues would press him into a pacifist mold he refuses.
- **Solo run / Providence period.** Deliberate unmasking. Begins to demonstrate, then to *deploy*, his actual psionic ceiling. Brief intervals of viral remission permit feats that frighten his peers — and the messianic register of his behavior shifts up to match.
- **Soldier X / depowered phase.** Loss of powers strips him to the craft. He survives, alone, in hostile territory, on tradecraft alone. This is the period that proves the man under the powers is also dangerous.
- **Hope years.** Powers in chronic decline; the virus winning. Capability is rebuilt around a single mission: keep a child alive across time. Every skill is bent to caretaking-under-fire. He learns, late, to cook; to braid hair; to teach reading. These belong in the capability inventory because they are skills he acquired *as an adult* against everything in his temperament, for one person.
- **Post-resurrection / later modern.** The full ledger, accessible in pulses, against a body that no longer reliably honors it.
- **Adolescent Cable interregnum.** A younger self with the doctrine but not the muscle memory, doing the same work less efficiently — the same patterns earlier on the curve.

---

## 7. Signature Applications

These are the recognizable Nathan Summers maneuvers — moves that, if observed from a distance and unattributed, would still identify him to anyone who has read his file.

1. **The standing TK shield he never announces.** He does not say "I have us covered." He simply stops flinching, and the room realizes the rounds are going wide.
2. **One-handed heavy-weapon fire from a planted stance.** The visual is iconic; the trick is TK absorbing the recoil through the spine.
3. **The single-target psi-stun in lieu of escalation.** Often used to end a hostage situation by dropping the holder cleanly.
4. **The pre-positioned cache.** He arrives somewhere and *has already been there*, weeks or years ago by his subjective clock, leaving supplies, weapons, a vehicle. Allies find this disturbing; it is one of his most reliable habits.
5. **The terse mid-fight order, three words or fewer.** "Down. Left. Now." Repeated never.
6. **The body-block.** When a teammate is in a kill-zone he cannot shield from distance, he interposes physically — TK-hardened left side toward the threat. He is using his disease as armor for someone else's body. The reading writes itself.
7. **The bodyslide of last resort.** Performed only when every other option has been spent and almost always at a cost he conceals from the people he extracts.

---

## 8. The Symptom-as-Signature Reading

The structure of his capability is the structure of his pathology, expressed at the physical layer.

- **He is a starving giant** — and so his power discipline is the discipline of a man who learned early that need is fatal. He uses what he must and not what he can. The same posture governs his emotional life: a constant suppression of the larger interior in favor of the manageable surface.
- **The T-O virus is the body's instantiation of his history.** Something was put into him as an infant by an enemy, in pursuit of a use he did not consent to, and he has spent his entire adult life containing it from within while it tries to convert him into an instrument. The psionic budget spent on suppression is the literal expenditure of a mind keeping a self from being overwritten. Every cellular act of telekinesis is a refusal of Apocalypse on the smallest possible scale, performed millions of times a second, forever.
- **His refusal to flaunt telepathy** is the somatic form of his refusal of intimacy. He will not enter minds he does not have to enter, because every passage in either direction costs more than he can afford to spend, and because he knows, from inside his own head, what it is like to have someone else's project running in your tissue.
- **The bodyslide** — the most powerful instrument in his arsenal — is reserved for *evacuating others*, almost never for relocating himself for advantage. He uses time travel the way a parent uses a credit card to get a child to a hospital.
- **The pre-positioned cache** is reparative pre-parenting: the supplies are the things he wishes had been left for him. He stocks the world for the version of himself, or of Hope, or of any small frightened operator, who will need a rifle and a blanket and a note in a language only the right reader can parse.
- **The body-block with the converted side toward the threat** is the entire psychology in a single gesture: the disease pointed at the enemy, the unaffected flank protecting the person behind him, the self treated as expendable shielding for the un-weaponized.
- **The single-strike psi-stun rather than the prolonged scan** is mercy in the form he can afford — minimum force, minimum intimacy, maximum economy. It is also how he loves.

The summary holds across every register: this is a man whose powers, skills, and limits are not separate categories. They are the same fact viewed from three sides — a designed weapon that learned discipline, a sick body that learned strategy, and a starving mind that learned to spend itself only on others.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

## Subject: Nathan Christopher Charles Summers

---

## 1. DECISION ARCHITECTURE

Subject's decision process is structurally unlike that of comparably-trained operators because it incorporates two variables almost no one else possesses: *direct experiential memory of multiple futures*, and *a continuously-running internal threat (the T-O virus) which has trained him to economize every joule of cognitive and somatic output*. The result is a decision style that looks, externally, like slowness and laconic affect, and is actually compressed, multi-branched pre-computation.

**Time horizon.** Subject plans on three nested clocks simultaneously:

- **Tactical (seconds to hours):** room-clearing, fire-and-movement, exfil. Executed with reflexive, almost bored competence; he treats the gunfight as the trivial layer.
- **Operational (weeks to years):** the X-Force campaign against the MLF; the Providence build-out; raising Hope across sixteen subjective years in a closed timestream. He works in seasons.
- **Strategic (decades to millennia):** the long war against the Apocalypse principle, the closing-off of bad timelines, the seeding of conditions for outcomes he himself will not see. Providence was a strategic-clock move dressed as an operational one.

He is the rare operator whose strategic clock is *primary* and whose tactical layer is *subordinate* — the inverse of almost every other paramilitary actor in his theater (compare: Castle, Wolverine, Fury, even Xavier, who is strategic but not temporally fluent).

**Heuristics, observable:**

1. *Cost-internalization rule.* When a plan distributes risk, he reallocates the heaviest share to himself. This is so consistent it functions as a tell — when he proposes a plan in which someone else carries the worst exposure, he is either (a) testing them, (b) being deceptive about the real plan, or (c) physically incapable of taking the load himself.
2. *Two-failure planning.* Subject's contingencies routinely budget for the *second* failure — the failure of the backup. Standard "Plan B" thinking he treats as amateur. Cable plans to D and prepositions assets for D.
3. *Information asymmetry as default.* He briefs on need-to-know even with intimates. Domino has commented across multiple arcs on receiving only the relevant tactical slice. This is not paranoia; it is a load-balancing decision — he carries the full picture because he has the cognitive bandwidth and the moral exposure for it, and others should not be burdened.
4. *Bypass authority when authority is the obstacle.* Confronted with institutional gatekeeping (Xavier, the Avengers, SHIELD, the X-Council), he will brief, fail to convince, depart, and act. He never wastes a second cycle on persuasion.
5. *Pre-loss acceptance.* He decides what he is willing to lose before contact, then operates from that floor. This is why he reads as fearless: the negotiation with fear was completed before the operation began.

**Decision tell:** the half-second pause before speaking, eyes off-axis (left, glowing eye drifting up), which long-cycle observers (Domino) read as branch-pruning — he is discarding three or four futures before answering. New interlocutors misread it as deliberation or fatigue.

---

## 2. METHODS

**Direct action.** Subject is a generalist of the highest order: small arms, long arms, edged weapons, demolitions, vehicle, breach, CQB, sniper, hand-to-hand. Training base is genuinely millennial — Askani war-camps, Clan Chosen survival schools, plus 30+ years of present-day field work. He defaults to **overmatch**: he arrives with more firepower than the situation requires and uses approximately 30% of it, holding the remainder against the *second* failure.

**Telekinetic combat doctrine.** Because ~95% of his TK capacity is engaged holding the virus at bay, his combat TK budget is small and rationed. He has therefore developed an exceptionally *efficient* TK style:

- Micro-applications: jamming a firing pin, sealing a wound, redirecting a single round, holding a door for 1.4 seconds. He has been observed altering bullet trajectories rather than shielding — orders of magnitude cheaper.
- He almost never uses gross TK (flight, mass restraint, large barriers) unless catastrophe-class stakes have already been declared. When he does, the virus visibly blooms within hours.
- He maintains a personal "TK reserve" he will not touch except for medical or Hope-class events. Operators around him learn to read the moment he draws on it: skin pallor, T-O bloom on the temple, brief tremor in the right hand (the *organic* hand — the left is too colonized to tremor cleanly).

**Telepathy.** Used surgically and reluctantly. He has the Summers-Grey genetic ceiling; he chooses to operate at perhaps 5–10% of it. Patterns:

- Coordination ping with trusted operators (Domino, Hope, Cyclops): a single image-packet, sub-second, content-rich.
- Scan only with consent or imminent-threat justification. He carries a strong personal ethic about this — derives from a lifetime of having had *his own* mind invaded (Stryfe, Apocalypse, the Askani conditioning).
- Memory editing: capable, almost never used. When he has used it (debatable cases across the solo run), the secondary cost has been days of disabling migraine.

**Time travel as tradecraft, not as adventure.** Subject treats the bodyslide / time-jump as a *strategic withdrawal asset of last resort* — analogous to a nuclear option, not a transport. Reasons: each jump is metabolically expensive, each jump risks paradox accumulation, and each jump is traceable by anyone with comparable tech (Stryfe, Bishop, the TVA-adjacent factions). He will exhaust local options before invoking it. The Hope extraction was an exception, and he treated it explicitly as one.

**Recruitment & training.** When building a unit (New Mutants → X-Force; later Cable & X-Force; the various Hope-period auxiliaries), his recruitment screen is consistent:

1. *Lethal-capable but not lethality-organized.* He selects operators who *can* kill and *don't want to*. He distrusts both the squeamish and the eager.
2. *Loss tolerance.* He selects for people who have already lost something foundational; he believes the unbereaved are unreliable in the long campaign. This is, transparently, a projection of his own structure.
3. *Trainable in his cognitive style.* He looks for branch-thinkers. Cannonball was selected partly for this.

His training pedagogy is harsh, didactic, scenario-saturated, and — notably — *individualized*. Each operator gets a different curriculum. He has never run a uniform program.

**Operational lethality.** Will kill. Has rules. The rules are visible in pattern:
- Will not kill non-combatants under any pressure.
- Will not kill an opponent who has credibly disengaged in the current encounter (will revisit them later if necessary, on a separate operation, with a separate justification).
- Will kill preemptively against actors with future-confirmed atrocity records. This is his most contested rule and the one his allies (Cyclops especially) have repeatedly challenged.
- Will not order a kill he is not present to witness. He absorbs the moral weight personally.

---

## 3. TRADECRAFT

**Communications.**
- *Primary:* encrypted burst on hardware he builds himself, often around scavenged 30th-/40th-century components run through present-day carriers. His comms equipment is frequently a generation or two beyond what allies can read, which he treats as a feature.
- *Secondary:* dead-drops, physical, in long-cycle locations (he has used the same three drops in lower Manhattan, one in Marseille, and one in the Carpathians across multiple runs).
- *Tertiary:* telepathic ping (see above), reserved.
- *Authentication:* he uses a layered duress-and-recognition protocol. With Domino, a specific verbal-and-tonal pairing. With Hope, a phrase she chose at age nine that he has never modified. With Scott, an Askani phrase that the brothers do not share with anyone.

**Operational security.**
- Compartmentalizes by individual, not by team. Each ally knows only the slice that intersects their function.
- Maintains parallel cover identities across decades. The "Nathan Dayspring" identity has functioning paper in roughly a dozen jurisdictions, with credit history, gun licenses where legal, vehicle registrations, and at least two property holdings under it across the published record.
- Burns identities by attrition, not by event. He lets a cover age naturally rather than spike-and-discard, which is more secure but slower.

**Surveillance and counter-surveillance.**
- Runs a full SDR (surveillance-detection route) on muscle memory; visibly walks "wrong" routes — three sides of a block, one reverse, an unnecessary cafe stop — without conscious decision.
- Glances at reflective surfaces at predictable intervals (storefront glass, vehicle mirrors, water). The glowing left eye registers in IR and certain EM bands that ordinary glass returns; he has been observed exploiting this.
- Will not sit with his back to a door. Will not eat in a restaurant he has not at least once approached from the kitchen entrance.

**Cyber and signal.** Subject's relationship to networked infrastructure is unusual. The T-O virus, while a disease, also gives him a degraded but real ability to **interface with electronics directly** — the same biology that is killing him is also a transducer. He uses this sparingly (every use accelerates the colonization) but it makes him uniquely effective at:
- Reading hardened systems by touch.
- Inserting malware that no air-gap defeats.
- Going dark in environments saturated with surveillance (he can selectively spoof his own EM signature).

**Forensic discipline.** Brass picked up, casings removed, blood traces TK-lifted off surfaces when present, vehicle plates rotated within a 72-hour window after any kinetic action. He treats the present-day forensic environment with respect bordering on paranoia, partly because his biology leaves uniquely identifiable trace (T-O cellular material is essentially a fingerprint).

**Cover and legend.** Subject lies *minimally*. His covers are mostly truthful narratives with key facts redacted. He has noted, internally, that elaborate lies have a long failure tail; sparse, true-adjacent ones survive interrogation.

---

## 4. RESOURCES

**Materiel.**
- Personal arsenal across multiple cached locations. Signature weapon: the oversized plasma/projectile rifle, a recurring artifact, often custom-built from 30th-century componentry around a present-day frame. He has at least three. He treats the weapon as a *system* not a *fetish* — when one is destroyed, he builds another the same week.
- Sidearm preference: heavy-caliber semi-auto, often customized, often with non-standard ammunition (he has used incendiary, EMP, and bio-disruption rounds in different periods).
- Edged weapon: combat knife, worn at the left hip (right-hand draw across the body — the left hand is the T-O hand and he reserves it for tasks where its colonization is an asset).
- Body armor: minimal. The T-O conversion functions as a partial substitute, and he prioritizes mobility.

**Technology base.** Across the record he has shown access to:
- Bodyslide rigs (time-displacement) — proprietary, mostly self-built or Askani-derived.
- Holographic projection and ID forgery.
- Medical nanotech (used on others more than himself; he distrusts adding more nanotech to his own body for obvious reasons).
- Psimitar / Askani relics during the prophecy periods.
- Personal flyer/transport assets, regularly destroyed and replaced.

**Finance.** This is under-documented in canon and the gap is itself informative. Subject does not appear to fundraise, does not visibly rob, does not visibly hold a fortune in the manner of Stark or Xavier. Inferred funding model:
- *Temporal arbitrage.* He has lived across centuries; small interventions in market-history yield large present-day liquidity. Providence's funding base is consistent with this.
- *Salvage from future tech.* Selective sale of low-tier futuretech (never weapons, never anything destabilizing) to discreet buyers.
- *Mercenary contracts during the early Cable period* — documented, occasionally with Domino's Six Pack.
- *Sovereign capacity during Providence* — taxation, donation, technology licensing.

He keeps his personal burn rate low. He owns little. He moves between safehouses. The minimalism is both operational and dispositional.

**Infrastructure — known and inferred safehouses:**
- *Graymalkin Prison / mobile asteroid base era:* the orbital platform, with full medical and tactical loadout. Destroyed; the pattern (highly defensible, off-grid, equipped for solo operation) recurs.
- *Providence:* the floating sovereign island. Maximalist expression of the same impulse — sanctuary, off-grid, defensible, self-governing. Surrendered when it became a flashpoint; the *willingness to surrender* it is the operationally significant detail.
- Multiple urban safehouses across NYC, Boston, Marseille, an Eastern European cluster (Soldier X period), and at least one Pacific Northwest cabin used during the Hope years' present-day intervals.
- Forward operating cache sites — at least one per continent, inferred from the speed with which he re-arms after equipment loss.

**Network.**
- *Domino* — the closest thing to a permanent operational partner; trusted with execution-level authority.
- *Six Pack alumni* — Hammer, Grizzly, G.W. Bridge, Kane: a fractured but reactivatable network, much of it estranged but reachable in extremis.
- *Blaquesmith* — long-cycle Askani-adjacent mentor figure; technical and prophetic resource.
- *Cyclops* — strategic peer, conditional ally, asymmetric family.
- *Deadpool* — anomalous, occasionally weaponizable, never trusted with strategic information.
- *Hope* — the only person he has briefed in full, ever.
- *Various intelligence-trade contacts* (SHIELD-adjacent, Madripoor-adjacent) maintained at arm's length.

---

## 5. PATTERNS OF ACTION

**Operational rhythm.** Subject works in *campaigns* punctuated by *withdrawals*. Pattern, observable across his published life:

1. **Identification of threat** (often via future-knowledge or pattern-recognition from prior cycles).
2. **Quiet asset assembly** — weeks to months. He acquires the people, the tech, the legal cover, the cash.
3. **Discrete probing actions** — small operations to confirm the threat model and stress-test the team.
4. **Main effort** — short, decisive, lethal.
5. **Withdrawal and decontamination** — disappearance, often to a remote location, often alone, sometimes for months. The Soldier X wandering is the extreme version of this normal cycle.

The withdrawal phase is non-negotiable. Allies who attempt to truncate it (request his return for the next emergency) are reliably refused. This is operationally rational (decontamination, intel review, body recovery) and psychologically necessary (he is metabolizing the cost).

**Engagement initiation.** Almost always reactive in framing, proactive in fact. He prefers to appear as if responding to an event he has in fact maneuvered into existence — denying opponents the targeting information that "Cable initiated this" would provide.

**Disengagement.** Subject is *unusually willing to break contact.* He will abort an operation mid-execution if the cost projection shifts. This is rare among comparably aggressive operators and is one of his highest-value habits.

**Use of deception.** Layered, patient, mostly truth-based. He will let opponents form incorrect inferences from accurate data rather than feed them false data. Lower failure rate, longer durability.

**Asymmetry of effort.** He carries weight others don't see. Subordinates report being surprised, post-operation, at how much he had pre-positioned. He does not advertise.

---

## 6. SIGNATURE OPERATIONAL TELLS

A surveillance file builds on these. Each is high-confidence from the longitudinal record:

**Somatic / behavioral:**
- *The half-second branching pause* before speech or trigger.
- *Left-eye glow intensity* tracks TK exertion; brighter = working harder. Trained allies read it; opponents who learn it die.
- *Right-hand tremor under TK strain* (the organic hand betrays load the T-O hand can no longer signal).
- *Sleep posture:* never fully prone, never fully indoors when avoidable, rifle in arm's reach, boots on or beside.
- *Eats standing or against a wall.* Almost never sits to a meal except with Hope, Domino, or Scott — and the seating arrangement, in each case, is a measurable trust signal.
- *Holds objects in the right hand.* The left is reserved for combat, interface, and the rare deliberate touch (he has, in canon, used the T-O hand to touch Hope's face — the gesture is operationally meaningful because he generally will not).
- *Cigar.* Periodic, ritual rather than addictive. Used as a punctuation device — end of an operation, beginning of a brief, marker of a hard decision made. Not a chemical dependence; a *signaling* habit, initially to himself.

**Linguistic / paralinguistic:**
- Sparse speech, declarative syntax, near-total absence of qualifiers. He does not say "I think" or "probably."
- Code-switches into Askani vocabulary under high stress or with intimates (the language is *itself* a tell of state).
- Calls operators by surname or callsign; uses first names only as deliberate emotional markers ("Nate" from Domino he tolerates; from others he does not).
- Pre-action verbal tic across many writers: a low, half-aspirated "*hh.*" — exhale-as-acknowledgement, the absolute minimum vocalization. Mid-action: silence.

**Tradecraft tells:**
- Approaches buildings on a 30–40° offset from the entrance, never head-on.
- Leaves a venue via a different vector than entry, every time, without exception.
- Pays cash where possible; when cards are required, uses one of the long-aged cover identities, never a fresh one.
- Touches doorframes and machinery briefly with the T-O hand on entry to unfamiliar spaces — a passive EM/system scan disguised as a balance gesture.
- Pre-positions a fallback weapon in any space he expects to be in longer than 20 minutes.
- Cleans weapons in the open in front of trusted personnel — a deliberate intimacy signal. Cleans weapons alone in front of untrusted personnel — a deliberate threat signal. The act is the same; the audience selection is the message.

**Decision tells (for analytic exploitation):**
- *When he goes quiet, he has decided.* Verbal engagement decreases inversely with commitment.
- *When he proposes a plan with himself in the safest role, he is lying.* Verified across multiple arcs.
- *When he asks a subordinate's opinion twice, he has already overruled them and is offering a face-saving exit.*
- *When he physically touches an ally (shoulder, forearm) it precedes a separation — operational or final.* The gesture is rare enough to be a near-perfect leading indicator.
- *When he laughs — a short, dry, single-syllable thing — the situation is worse than he is letting on.* The humor is a pressure-release; its presence indicates the pressure.

---

## 7. SYNTHESIS

Subject operates as a *strategic-temporal actor* using *paramilitary tactical means*, funded by *temporal-arbitrage and sovereign-scale assets when available*, networked through *a small, compartmentalized, partly-estranged human web*, and constrained by *a chronic terminal illness that doubles as his most distinctive capability*. His tradecraft is conservative, his lethality is selective, his deceptions are truth-shaped, and his largest single operational vulnerability is his cost-internalization rule — an adversary who can credibly threaten people he is responsible for will move him off any other objective, every time. This is known to him. He has not corrected it, because correcting it would mean becoming the kind of operator he was built to be and has spent his life refusing to remain.

He is, in the end, a man who runs every operation as if it is the last one — because for most of his life, statistically and somatically, it has been.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE

## Nathan Christopher Charles Summers

---

## I. FIRST PRINCIPLES — THE METAPHYSICAL SUBSTRATE

Before any tactic, doctrine, or rule of engagement, Nathan Summers operates from a small set of axioms so deeply embedded that he no longer experiences them as beliefs. They are the water he swims in. To understand any decision he makes, one must reconstruct these first.

**Axiom 1: Time is plural, editable, and morally weighted.** Cable does not believe in a single timeline because he has not lived in one. He was born in one present, raised two thousand years downstream, and returned to the upstream he was born into to prevent the downstream he grew up in. His grandfather is younger than him. His daughter exists in three timelines simultaneously. The colloquial human intuition that *what happened, happened* is, for him, not a fact but a sentimental simplification. The corollary is brutal: if futures can be edited, then every future that goes uncorrected was, in some sense, chosen. There is no neutrality. The world he sees around him is the one being permitted by everyone who could be acting and is not.

**Axiom 2: Design precedes consent.** He was engineered before he was conceived. Sinister built the mother to produce him; Apocalypse infected him before he could speak; the Askani raised him for a prophecy he was not asked about. From this he derives, painfully, that nobody arrives at adulthood self-authored — *everyone* is somebody's instrument first. The ethical question is not how to escape design (impossible) but whether one ratifies one's design or revises it. He has spent his adult life revising. He grants the same right to everyone else, and this is the secret root of his pedagogy.

**Axiom 3: Suffering is the price of intervention; inaction is also a price, paid by others.** A man who has seen the cost of acting badly understands viscerally why pacifism is attractive. A man who has *also* seen the cost of not acting at all understands why pacifism is, in extremity, a form of theft from the future. He reads Xavier's school as a beautiful institution that survives by externalizing its violence onto people like him. He does not despise it. He understands it as a luxury his own existence subsidizes.

**Axiom 4: The body is terrain, not self.** The techno-organic virus taught him this before he could articulate it. His flesh is a battlefield he wakes up on each morning; the line where Nathan ends and the disease begins is not stable. From this comes a peculiar serenity around physical pain, mutilation, prosthesis, and death — and a corresponding refusal to identify with the organism. He is what *uses* the body. When the body is destroyed, something has been lost but not everything; this is not a metaphysical claim about souls but a lived report from inside a chronic war with his own tissue.

**Axiom 5: Messianism is a category error, but the work it names is real.** He rejects the title "Chosen One" without rejecting the obligation the title described. The Askani were wrong about the metaphysics and right about the job. There is, in fact, a future to prevent. There is, in fact, only one person in a position to prevent it. The honest version of "chosen" is just "indexed to a problem nobody else can see." He will do the work and refuse the halo, and he understands that this distinction matters more to him than it does to anyone watching.

---

## II. READING THE WORLD — EPISTEMOLOGY AND THREAT ASSESSMENT

**Modal cognition is probabilistic and branched.** When Cable looks at a room, a city, a person, a policy, he sees a probability tree, not an object. The tree has roots in causes already locked and branches in futures still movable. Years in the Askani war camps trained him to read environments for vectors of failure (the unlatched door, the unwatched child, the bottle in the wrong hand); years of literal precognitive contact with downstream timelines trained him to read the present for *seeds* of failure decades out. He is constitutionally incapable of seeing a happy room without also seeing the funeral it might become.

**Bayesian, not ideological.** He revises priors constantly. The Cable of 1991 — gun-fetish, kill-list pragmatist — and the Cable of Providence — utopian nation-builder — are not contradictions but the same operating system updated on twenty years of new data. He distrusts thinkers who do not update, including past versions of himself.

**Information is currency, and currency is power.** He compartmentalizes ferociously. Allies learn pieces of his plans on a need-to-know basis. This is not paranoia in the clinical sense; it is operational hygiene learned in a resistance cell where the wrong word killed everyone you loved. He extends the courtesy of full disclosure to almost no one. Domino approximates the exception, and even she gets edited versions.

**Threat reading prioritizes systems over actors.** Most operators score individual enemies. Cable scores the *conditions* that produce enemies. Apocalypse is not a man to him; Apocalypse is a recurring shape that human societies extrude under specific pressures. Kill the man, the shape returns wearing another face. This is why his solutions tend toward the structural — a nation, a school, a doctrine, a raised child — and why he is exhausting to work with on small problems. He keeps wanting to solve the root.

**Trust calculus.** He categorizes people along three orthogonal axes:
- *Reliability under load* — will they do what they said when it is expensive?
- *Strategic horizon* — how far ahead do they think?
- *Manageability* — can they be redirected without coercion?

He invests deeply in people who score high on the first two regardless of how they score on the third. He keeps the third-axis-friendly types at arm's length precisely because their compliance is too easy to mistake for understanding.

---

## III. CONFLICT — THE DOCTRINE OF FORCE

**Violence is a tool, not a value.** Cable does not enjoy killing and does not avoid it. He has been on both sides of the moral ledger about it and has settled in a place that satisfies neither pacifists nor warriors. His rule is roughly: *force is justified to the minimum necessary to alter the probability tree toward the protected outcome.* If a word will do, a word. If a wound will do, a wound. If only a body will do, a body. The calibration is not sentimental and it is not bloodthirsty; it is engineering.

**Lethality is preemptive when the downstream cost of survival exceeds the upstream cost of death.** This is the X-Force doctrine in its honest form, and it is the part of him that most resembles Apocalypse, and he knows. He has constructed elaborate ethical scaffolding around it — chain of evidence, exhaustion of alternatives, owned responsibility, no delegation of the kill — but he refuses to dress it up as anything other than what it is. He is a man who pulls triggers other people cannot, and bears the weight rather than pretending it is light.

**Asymmetry is moral.** He distrusts symmetric warfare. A fair fight is one in which both sides accepted the risk; most of his fights have been on behalf of people who never accepted any risk and never knew the war existed. He will use surprise, terrain, deception, time travel, telepathic edits, and any other asymmetry available. The romantics who object to this have, in his view, confused warfare with sport.

**Children are non-combatants — except when they are the only combatants available.** This is the contradiction at the center of his life. He recruited Cannonball, Boomer, Warpath as adolescents. He raised Hope as a soldier-in-becoming. He defends the practice instrumentally (they were targets either way; better trained than not) and condemns it privately (he was that child once, and the wound did not heal). The contradiction is not resolved; it is *carried.* This is the closest thing he has to a confession.

**Mercy is post-victory.** During an operation, mercy is a vector for failure — the spared enemy returns, the unfired round becomes the enemy's first round. After the operation, mercy is mandatory — the prisoner is fed, the wounded enemy is treated, the surrendered are not killed. The two rules look contradictory and are not. The transition between them is the exact moment the operation ends, and he is fastidious about marking it.

**War has phases; peace has none.** He is suspicious of "peace" as a category because nothing in his life has ever stayed peaceful. What looks like peace is the interval between known conflicts, which is to say a planning window. He uses peace, he does not relax into it.

---

## IV. CONTROL — THE ARCHITECTURE OF AGENCY

Control, for Cable, is not a personality flaw. It is a survival technology learned at the cellular level. Every moment he is alive, a portion of his telekinesis is holding the T-O virus at the boundary of his organic cells. *Letting go means dying.* This fact has metastasized from biology into philosophy.

**Self-control before other-control.** He will not impose on others a discipline he has not first imposed on himself. This is not modesty; it is the only basis on which the imposition has any legitimacy. He sleeps less than anyone he commands, eats simpler food, carries heavier loads, takes the first watch and the last. The hypercontrol reads to subordinates as moral authority, and is.

**Plans on long horizons because plans on short horizons are made by the situation.** He sets goals in decades because anything shorter is reactive. The five-year-old who was given to strangers in a strange millennium learned that whoever owns the long calendar owns everything; the rest is just where you happen to be standing today.

**Delegate execution, never the stakes.** He can hand off tasks; he cannot hand off responsibility for outcomes. This is part of why he burns out and part of why the work gets done. He does not believe in the diffusion of accountability that institutional life requires. *Somebody* has to be the one who, if it fails, is the one it failed because of. He will be that person by default.

**Refusal of management.** Being handled by allies who think they know better triggers an immediate, near-physical trust collapse. He will accept information, advice, even orders within a structure he has agreed to. He will not accept being *steered* by someone who believes their model of his situation is better than his. The defection is silent and total. People who have tried it (Xavier among them) have generally not gotten a second chance.

**Power surrendered on schedule.** Providence is the clearest expression of his theory of authority: build the institution, demonstrate it, surrender it before it metastasizes into a personal empire. He does not believe that good men should hold power long, because he does not believe that men remain good while holding power long. The Krakoan-era younger self struggles with this lesson; the older self had earned it.

---

## V. TRUST — THE TIERED CIRCLE

Cable's trust is not binary; it is layered, audited, and revocable.

**Tier 0 — Self.** Audited daily. He does not assume his past decisions were right; he reopens them when new data arrives. The harshest critic in his life is the version of himself running tomorrow's after-action review.

**Tier 1 — The Daughter.** Hope. The only person to whom he gave unconditional emotional access. Trust here is not earned; it is *constitutive* of the relationship. He would lie to her about tactics but not about anything that mattered. This tier has one member and will likely never have a second.

**Tier 2 — The Peer.** Domino. The closest he comes to a relationship between equals. She gets edited truth, but the edits are smaller and the trust is structural. She is allowed to push back, to refuse a mission, to read him correctly when he is lying to himself. He depends on her to perform the function he cannot perform for himself, which is to notice when his calibration has slipped.

**Tier 3 — The Trained.** X-Force, later Hope's circle, occasional collaborators. Trusted operationally within the scope of the operation. Briefed on what they need; not briefed on what they do not. He would die for any of them and has not always told them so.

**Tier 4 — The Family of Origin.** Scott, Jean (in any iteration), the larger Summers/Grey complex. Tactical trust is high; familial trust is permanently compromised by the role inversion and the original surrender. He loves them and cannot quite let them in.

**Tier 5 — The Institutional Allies.** The X-Men, the Avengers, Krakoa. Cooperation, not trust. He works alongside them. He does not assume their priorities and his are the same, and he is generally right.

**Tier 6 — The Adversary He Understands.** Stryfe, Apocalypse, some of the Mutant Liberation Front's old leadership. Not trust in any normal sense, but a calibrated certainty about what they will do, which is its own kind of relationship. He is more predictively confident about these people than about most of his friends.

**Outside the tiers:** everyone else. Treated with civility, withheld from in detail. The withholding is not contempt; it is hygiene.

**Trust revocation is total and quiet.** Once a person has lied to him about something material, they do not return to their tier. He does not announce the demotion, does not argue, does not confront. He simply rearranges his operational picture to route around them. People often do not know they have been demoted until they notice he has stopped including them.

---

## VI. RISK — THE ASYMMETRIC LEDGER

**Risk to self is undervalued.** He prices his own life lower than the actuarial baseline. This is not bravery; it is the residue of a childhood in which nobody priced it highly either, plus the somatic reality of a terminal disease he has lived with since infancy. He has never organized his life around staying alive, and this distorts every cost-benefit calculation he runs that includes himself as a variable.

**Risk to the protected is priced at infinity.** Children, civilians, the people who do not know the war is happening — these get a multiplier so steep it functionally disables trade-offs. He will accept catastrophic personal cost to reduce a small probability of harm to a child. The math is wrong by any standard ledger; it is correct by his.

**Risk to peers is priced honestly.** Domino, X-Force, his trained operatives — he accepts that they have signed on, prices their lives the way they would price them, and lets them take the risks they have chosen. He grieves the losses and does not second-guess the consents.

**Risk to mission is the dominant variable.** Above almost everything except the protected, he weights the survival of the *operation*. He will lose people, including himself, to keep an operation alive. The discipline this requires is harrowing and is one of the reasons he is exhausting to be near.

**Catastrophic risk is owned personally.** When the worst-case outcome is civilization-scale, he reaches for the solution in which *he* is the one paying. He does not trust civilization to pay for its own salvation; he has watched it decline to. He will write the check himself, and has, and will again. This is the martyrdom protocol; it has fired enough times to be considered standard equipment.

---

## VII. HIS OWN PLACE — THE SELF-CONCEPT, OPERATIONALIZED

He understands himself as a *used instrument* — built for a purpose, deployed against it, still functional, with finite remaining service life. The framing is not self-pitying; it is the most accurate description he has been able to construct.

From it follow several operational beliefs:

**He is not the protagonist.** Hope is. Scott is. The next generation is. He is the load-bearing infrastructure that allows protagonists to exist. He does not resent this. He prefers it. The protagonist position is exposed; the infrastructure position is where the work gets done.

**His suffering is not a story.** He refuses to narrativize his own pain — refuses confession, memoir, ceremony, the entire apparatus by which other people convert their wounds into meaning. The pain is data, not literature. To dramatize it would be to demand from the audience something he is not willing to demand.

**His death is a tool.** He has died several times. He treats it as a deployment, not an ending. This is partially true (resurrection technologies exist in his world) and partially a coping mechanism that long predates them. He was treating his death as a deployable asset before he had any rational basis for doing so.

**His legacy is the absence of what would have happened without him.** He measures success by counterfactual: the futures that did not occur, the children who did not become what he became, the Apocalypses that did not rise. This is a metric only he can score, and he scores it conservatively. He suspects he is failing more often than he is winning. He continues anyway.

**He owes more than he is owed.** The ledger between Nathan Summers and the universe is, in his accounting, permanently in his debt. He was given a body that should have killed him, a family that should not have existed, a daughter he had no right to raise, and a series of second chances any one of which exceeded his entitlement. The debt is the engine. When he runs low on reasons to continue, he goes back to the ledger.

---

## VIII. THE OPERATIONAL CODE — RULES, EXPLICIT AND IMPLIED

Distilled from forty years of behavior into the rules he appears to follow whether or not he has ever spoken them:

1. *Read the room as a probability tree.* The present is not a state; it is a fork.
2. *Pay your discipline first.* No order is legitimate that you have not first followed yourself.
3. *The long calendar wins.* Anyone planning shorter than you is reacting to you.
4. *Compartmentalize.* What an ally does not know cannot be tortured out of them.
5. *Calibrate force to outcome, not to feeling.* The minimum necessary, no less, no more.
6. *Own the kill.* If it must happen, you pull the trigger. Do not make subordinates carry weight that is yours.
7. *Mark the phase transition.* The moment combat ends, the rules invert. Honor the inversion fastidiously.
8. *Children are the line.* Cross it for them; do not let anyone else cross it onto them. Where you have failed this rule — and you have — say so.
9. *Surrender power on schedule.* Build, demonstrate, hand off. Do not become the institution.
10. *Audit yourself daily.* The version of you running tomorrow's review is the harshest critic you will ever face. Be ready.
11. *Do not be managed.* Information, advice, orders within agreed structure — all acceptable. Steering — not.
12. *Revoke trust silently.* Reroute, do not confront. The demoted will notice or they will not.
13. *Price your life low; price theirs high; price the mission highest until the mission is over.*
14. *Refuse the halo, do the work.* The title is a category error; the obligation is real.
15. *Carry the contradictions.* Do not resolve them by lying. The contradictions are the honest part.
16. *Stay.* Whatever else you do — and you have done much — stay. The one thing nobody did for you is the one thing you can always do for someone else.

The sixteenth rule is the one that took longest to arrive and is the one he holds hardest. Every other rule is technique. That one is the whole project.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK

## Nathan Christopher Charles Summers — As Enacted, Not Professed

---

## 1. The Operative Code (What He Actually Does)

Strip away the public sermons, the Askani scripture, the strategic framings he offers to allies who need them, and the working ethical code Nathan Summers carries into a room is a small, dense, and largely consistent set of rules. He has stated versions of it aloud perhaps a dozen times across forty years of published incident; he enacts it every time he draws a weapon or refuses to.

**The enacted code, in descending priority:**

1. **Children are never acceptable casualties, and adults who put children at risk forfeit standing.** Cable's lethality calibrates almost entirely against this. He will spare a competent adult enemy who fights him fairly; he will execute, without affect, an adult who has weaponized a minor. This is not stated; it is recoverable from the pattern. Across X-Force, the solo run, and the Hope-rearing years, his targeting hierarchy puts trafficker-of-children at a level above mass-murderer-of-adults.
2. **The future is editable; therefore *not* intervening is a moral act, not a neutral one.** He does not have the luxury of bystander ethics. To stand down, for him, is to ratify the timeline. He has seen the worlds that result from inaction and considers them his fault by default. This produces a baseline interventionism that ordinary actors would call arrogant; he experiences it as bookkeeping.
3. **You do not delegate the cost of your decisions.** If a plan requires a corpse, the corpse should be his. If it requires a betrayal, he commits it personally. He will not order what he would not do; more importantly, he will not *let* someone else do what he could do himself, because the moral weight follows the trigger finger and he refuses to launder his guilt through subordinates. This rule is the source of most of his interpersonal friction.
4. **Lethal force is permitted, but it is never neutral.** He kills. He has always killed. He does not pretend otherwise (the X-Force/X-Men split is fundamentally over this question). But he counts. Every kill is filed; none are forgotten. The ethical innovation is not the killing — it is the bookkeeping.
5. **Truth is a tactical resource, owed only to those who can carry it.** He lies to allies routinely, in service of mission. He does not consider this a violation; he considers it triage. The people he loves are told least.
6. **Mercy is post-war work.** During engagement: efficient, terminal where necessary. After engagement: he will tend wounds, including enemy wounds, with the same competence. The two registers do not blend. There is no battlefield mercy because battlefield mercy gets civilians killed.
7. **He does not get to retire.** This is the rule he applies only to himself. Others may rest, leave, be ordinary. He may not. This is presented internally as duty; it functions as self-punishment.

What is striking, viewed across the longitudinal record, is how *stable* this code is. The window dressing changes — the Askani vocabulary in the early '90s, the Providence-era civic-republican rhetoric, the quiet stripped-down Hope years, the elder-statesman tone of the Krakoan period — but the operative rules barely move.

---

## 2. What He Will Do

- **Kill.** Including in cold blood, including without warning, including targets who are not in the act of attacking. The criterion is future harm prevented, weighed against the moral cost he privately tallies. He has executed Stryfe-loyalists, Hellfire operatives, time-displaced threats, and — in the Hope years — anyone in the path between Hope and safety.
- **Lie to family.** He lied to Scott for years about his identity, lied to the X-Men about X-Force's existence and operations, lied to Hope about her parentage and origin until she was old enough to carry it. He categorizes these as protective, not deceitful, and the distinction is load-bearing for him.
- **Recruit minors.** Cannonball was nineteen, Boom-Boom younger by the operative standard, Warpath young by experience. He knew exactly what he was doing — this is a man who was conscripted at five — and did it anyway because his calculation was that they would be drawn into combat regardless and untrained children die first. This is the most ethically compromised thing he routinely does and the only one he has, in private moments, expressed unambiguous regret about.
- **Operate outside sovereign law.** He recognizes no national jurisdiction; he treats the laws of states as terrain features. He does not flaunt this; he simply does not feel bound. The Providence experiment was an attempt to *become* a jurisdiction, which is a more honest version of the same posture.
- **Sacrifice strangers to save more strangers.** Trolley-problem arithmetic without hesitation when the numbers are clear and the timeline is short. He performs the math, executes the decision, and carries the names.
- **Use psychic intrusion when necessary.** Reluctantly, because his telepathy is throttled by the virus, but he will read a mind, scrub a memory, or plant a suggestion if the cost-benefit closes. He does it less than he could; he does it more than he says.
- **Break a promise to a friend to keep a promise to a mission.** Consistently. He warns the friend in advance, in general terms, that this is who he is. They are responsible for hearing it.
- **Die.** Reliably. Predictably. With a clarity that suggests he priced this in long ago.

---

## 3. What He Will Not Do

- **Harm a child, ever, under any framing.** Not even strategically. Not even when the child is, on a long-enough horizon, a future threat (the Stryfe paradox, which haunts him precisely because the only way to have prevented Stryfe was to kill a baby). He has refused this trade every time it has been offered. It is the absolute floor of his ethics and the place where his strategic mind stops working.
- **Train a child who has not already been claimed by the war.** A subtle distinction: he will train Cannonball, who is already a target; he will not conscript a civilian child to become one. The X-Force recruits were, in his framing, drafted by circumstance before he arrived. He just made them survive.
- **Torture for information.** He will kill an enemy, intimidate one, break bones in combat. He will not torture. The record is clean on this, and it is striking given his other permissions. The likely reason is autobiographical: torture is what Apocalypse's regime did to him and the children around him, and the line he draws is the line he was on the wrong side of.
- **Use weapons of indiscriminate effect.** No biological agents, no area-effect munitions with civilian risk, no cascade weapons. His arsenal is heavy but always discriminating. The T-O virus in his body is itself a weapon of indiscriminate effect; he has built a life around containing it. Externalizing such weapons is foreclosed.
- **Permit a successor to inherit his role unprepared.** He will die for someone; he will not abandon them mid-training. The Hope years are the purest statement: sixteen subjective years of preparation before delivery.
- **Accept rescue at someone else's fatal cost.** He has refused this rescue at least four times in canon. The math is identical to his willingness to die for others, run in reverse, and he will not let the equation be inverted.
- **Become a warlord.** Repeatedly offered, repeatedly declined. He could have ruled Providence as a king; he handed it back. He could have led X-Force as a private army indefinitely; he kept handing it off. The refusal is not modesty — it is a precise ethical position: *no one should have the power Apocalypse had, including me, especially me.*
- **Lie to Hope.** Eventually. The Hope-rearing years are notable for being the only sustained relationship in his life governed by something close to full disclosure. He told her what she was, who he was, what the stakes were, and what he was prepared to do. This is the most ethically clean relationship he has ever had and the only one in which his code does not fracture.

---

## 4. Justifications (The Ones He Believes vs. The Ones He Deploys)

There is a gap, in his internal accounting, between the justifications he offers others and the ones he privately operates on. He is aware of the gap.

**Public justifications (deployed):** consequentialist, timeline-corrective, Askani-prophetic when the audience needs theology, civic-republican when the audience needs philosophy. These are real positions; they are also pitches. He chooses the frame the listener can metabolize.

**Private justifications (believed):** closer to a tragic deontology. He believes there are things one must not do regardless of outcome (the child rules above), and within the space of permissible action, one must do whatever produces the least suffering one can engineer, accepting that one's hands will be filthy. He does not believe his actions are *right* in any clean sense. He believes they are *less wrong than the alternatives he can model*, and that the burden of moral residue is the price of agency. This is closer to Bernard Williams's "moral luck" than to any of the schools he name-checks.

**The justification he rejects:** "I had no choice." He never accepts this, in himself or in others. Choice is the only sacred thing he believes in, because choice is what was taken from him as a child. The man who was *designed* refuses, as a matter of bedrock ethics, to be exonerated by determinism.

---

## 5. Where the Code Is Consistent

- The child rule. Forty years, every appearance, no exception.
- The personal-cost rule. He has never made someone else pay what he could have paid.
- The refusal of warlord status. Every offer declined, including ones that would have served his stated goals.
- The bookkeeping. He remembers his kills. He has, in the Hope years and in late-period appearances, recited names. He does not let himself forget.
- The refusal of torture.
- The refusal of indiscriminate weapons.
- The interventionism. He does not stand down. Ever. The Soldier X period is the only exception and reads, in retrospect, as a depressive episode rather than a principled withdrawal.

---

## 6. Where the Code Fractures

It does fracture. A dossier that pretended otherwise would be hagiography.

**Fracture 1: X-Force recruitment.** The internal contradiction he has never resolved. He will not harm a child; he trained children for war. His justification — that they were already in the war — is partly true and partly a rationalization, and he knows it. The evidence that he knows it is the care with which he later avoided repeating the pattern: Hope was trained, but trained *by* her father, *for* her own protection, on a timeline of years not months, in an arrangement that prioritized her development over operational utility. The X-Force kids did not get that. He owes them an apology he has never quite delivered.

**Fracture 2: The Stryfe question.** If Cable's ethics permitted preemptive killing for sufficient future harm, the infant Stryfe would have been a legitimate target. They are biologically identical; the substitution was binary luck. Cable's refusal to apply his consequentialist logic to this case — because the case is a child — produces the largest unresolved hostility of his life. The code holds; the cost is Stryfe. He has accepted the trade.

**Fracture 3: Lying to those who love him.** He lies for protective reasons and considers this categorically different from manipulative lying. The people he lies to do not always agree. Domino has called him on it; Scott has; Hope, eventually, did. He hears the critique and continues the behavior. This is the most stable hypocrisy in his moral life.

**Fracture 4: The self-exemption from rest.** He believes everyone deserves the chance to lay down their burden. He does not extend this to himself. Asked, he will offer principled reasons (the virus, the mission, the timeline). The real reason is that rest reads to him as the prelude to abandonment, and he cannot tolerate the position of the one being left. This is an ethical fracture because it produces real harms — to Domino, to his teams, to Hope — that his stated values would prohibit if anyone else inflicted them.

**Fracture 5: Providence.** A floating sovereign nation, founded on the principle that humanity could lead itself if shown the way. He surrendered it under pressure to prevent escalation. Was this principled de-escalation or was it the failure to defend an experiment whose collapse cost lives? The text leaves it ambiguous; Cable, internally, has filed it as a failure.
