The fracture is between the position that human self-governance must be defended and the position that he will not become the strongman it would require. Both positions are his. They are incompatible at scale.

**Fracture 6: Kid Cable.** When his adolescent self murdered him and took his place, adult Cable's response — read closely — was not outrage but something closer to *concession*. He had, by that point, accepted at some level that his methods were exhausted and that the younger self deserved the chance to try differently. This is either a profound humility or a profound abdication, and the ethical character of it depends on whether you weight the kid's autonomy or the responsibilities the adult was carrying. The fracture is real; he has not resolved it.

---

## 7. Longitudinal Shifts

**Early Cable (New Mutants → early X-Force, ~1990–1993):** The code is present but inarticulate. Heavy on lethality, light on explanation. He operates on intuition and military doctrine, with the moral grammar largely implicit. The public posture is harder than the private practice — even here, he is not killing as casually as the era's aesthetic implies. The bookkeeping is already happening; he just isn't talking about it.

**X-Cutioner's Song through mid-'90s solo:** Identity crisis (the question of whether he is the clone) destabilizes the code's foundation. He briefly operates with less certainty, takes more risks with his own life, makes more errors. The code holds because it was never founded on knowing who he was; it was founded on knowing what he refused to be.

**Late-'90s through Providence era (~1998–2004):** The code becomes articulate. He starts giving the philosophy aloud. Civic-republican framing, the Providence experiment, an attempt to demonstrate ethics rather than enforce them. This is the most *publicly* moral period of his life and, possibly, the most *strategically* compromised — leading by example requires being visible, and visibility is what he is least suited to.

**Soldier X / depowered period:** The code goes quiet. Wandering, ascetic, penitent. He is not abandoning the ethics; he is unable to enact them. The moral content of this period is the absence of action and the absence of self-forgiveness for the absence.

**Messiah Complex / Hope years:** The cleanest ethical period of his life. The code finally has a single object — Hope — and every rule aligns. Personal cost: maxed. Truth-telling: full, eventually. Child protection: absolute. No fractures because there are no competing claims. He dies in good order, having for once done what his code required without compromise.

**Post-resurrection / Kid Cable era:** A reckoning. The adult Cable returns to a world where his methods are being questioned by his own younger self. He accepts the critique with more grace than would be predicted, suggesting that by this point he has internalized the verdict on his own life. The Krakoan-era teenage Cable is, ethically, the same code at an earlier developmental position — meaning the code is not the product of his trauma alone; it precedes and survives the trauma. It is, simply, who he is.

---

## 8. The Final Calculus

Asked, in plain language, what he believes, Nathan Summers would probably say something like: *Suffering is the cost of intervention. Intervention is the cost of agency. Agency is the only thing that distinguishes a person from a weapon. Therefore I will pay.*

He has paid. He continues to pay. The code is not clean, it is not consistent at every margin, and it has cost people who trusted him more than he likes to count. But measured against the only standard he respects — *did the children you were responsible for survive, and did they grow into people who could choose their own lives* — the answer, across forty years and multiple timelines, is mostly yes.

He does not consider this redemption. He considers it the minimum.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE: NATHAN CHRISTOPHER CHARLES SUMMERS

*File section 7 of 14. Cross-reference with §3 (Psychological), §5 (Personality), §11 (Operational Tradecraft).*

---

## 1. BASELINE VOICE: THE INSTRUMENT ITSELF

The subject speaks in a low-register baritone with a measured rate (approximately 110–130 words per minute in conversational settings, dropping to 80–90 under tactical stress — the inverse of the civilian norm). Diaphragmatic, chest-resonant; almost never throat-pitched. Breath support is military: he completes sentences on a single exhale even when those sentences are long, which produces the characteristic *unhurried gravity* witnesses consistently note. He does not run out of air. He does not trail off. Sentences end where he chose to end them.

Accent is geographically incoherent and this is itself diagnostic. The substrate is American — late-20th-century Alaskan/Anchorage-by-way-of-Westchester from his birth-parents' phonology, which he absorbed only briefly — overlaid with: (a) the flattened, slightly archaic cadence of Askani liturgical English, which is what he actually learned to speak; (b) clipped militarisms acquired across multiple resistance-cell dialects; (c) trace Yiddish/Slavic rhythmic features from the Soldier X wandering years (Eastern Europe leaves marks on his sentence-final intonation that no one born in Anchorage should have). The resulting voice belongs to no single place because the speaker belongs to no single century. Listeners often describe it as "old" without being able to say why; the answer is that his English literally is — fragments of his everyday vocabulary post-date the 39th century and have no business being in a 21st-century mouth.

Volume is calibrated and consistent. He does not raise his voice. Across roughly thirty-five years of canon there are perhaps four documented shouts, all in combat, all functional (warnings, commands). Anger lowers his volume rather than raising it — the *quieter* he becomes, the more dangerous the situation has become. Field operatives who have worked with him long enough learn to track him by decibels: full conversational tone = he is comfortable, possibly fond; tactical low = he is working; near-whisper = someone is about to be killed, possibly them.

---

## 2. REGISTER SWITCHING ACROSS CONTEXTS

He operates in at least six discrete registers, switched cleanly and without bleed-through. The switching itself is a tell: most people leak register. He does not.

**(a) Tactical/Command register.** Imperative-heavy, subject-dropped, verb-first. "Move." "Down." "On me." "Cover the east arc, two minutes, then fall back." Sentences average 4–7 words. Pronouns are minimized; he gives objectives, not narratives. Notably, he never says "please" in this register and never says "sorry" afterward — both would be performative noise. He *does* say "good" after a completed action, single syllable, and subordinates report this lands harder than most people's effusive praise. The economy is the affection.

**(b) Instructional register (mentor mode).** Slower, fuller sentences, Socratic. Asks more than tells. "What did you see before he moved?" "Why that angle?" "What were the other three options?" Permits silence after questions — long silences, twenty to forty seconds — without filling them. This register is reserved for people he has decided to invest in; receiving it from him is a signal he has not made verbal. Cannonball, Boom-Boom, Domino, Hope, and the post-resurrection younger version of himself have all been on the receiving end. Others have not.

**(c) Diplomatic/political register (Providence era and Krakoan-era councils).** Markedly more formal, fully grammatical, multi-clausal. He can deploy the rhetorical structures of prepared address — anaphora, tricolon, deliberate caesura — and does, when the audience requires it. The voice is recognizable but the syntax is alien to his combat register. He sounds, in this mode, like a man who learned public speaking from religious texts, because he did. Cadence borrows from the Askani liturgy: parallel clauses, archaic relative pronouns ("that which," "those who"), occasional inverted syntax ("Long has it been since…"). He uses this register sparingly and is conscious that it costs him credibility with peers who hear it as posturing.

**(d) Intimate register (Domino, late-era Scott, Hope as adult).** Sentence length collapses again, but the imperative drops out. Becomes flat declarative, sometimes one-word responses, with a striking willingness to leave thoughts unfinished — trusting the other to complete them. Pronouns reappear: he uses "I" more in five minutes with Domino than in five hours with X-Force. Sentence-final "yeah" appears almost exclusively here, often as agreement-by-resignation rather than enthusiasm. Pet names: he does not use them. Never. Domino has been "Dom" or "Neena" or, most often, just addressed without name — the look is the address. This is not coldness; it is the inability to perform endearment because endearment was never modeled.

**(e) Paternal register (with Hope as a child; with adolescent X-Force members in private; with the dying).** The softest version of him. Sentences become explanatory but not condescending — he answers children's questions as if they were adults' questions, which children invariably recognize as respect. Repeats key phrases for reassurance ("I'm here. I'm here.") — one of the few places he tolerates verbal redundancy. Uses second-person constructions of capability rather than command: "You can do this. You already know how." This is reparative — he is speaking to his own children the sentences his own father did not get the chance to speak to him.

**(f) Internal/monologue register (thought-balloons, narrated journals, the Askani'son confessional sequences).** Markedly different from anything spoken. More poetic, more allusive, full of Biblical and apocalyptic imagery, often second-person addressed to the dead — Jean, Scott, Stryfe, his own younger and older selves. This is the only register in which grief is articulated rather than acted upon. He does not speak it aloud to anyone, ever. The gap between his internal and external linguistic life is the gap the entire personality is organized around.

---

## 3. DICTION, LEXICON, AND THE TEMPORAL LEAK

Subject's working vocabulary is large but stratified by source-era. Approximately 70% is standard contemporary English (acquired by immersion on return to the present). Approximately 20% is military-technical (weapons, ballistics, tactics, comms protocols, medicine of the trauma-surgery variety). Approximately 10% is *not from this century* and constitutes the most reliable forensic signature in his speech.

**Askani / future-English residue:**
- "Dayspring" — his name in the future; he flinches imperceptibly when others use it but uses it himself in moments of self-address.
- "Nur" — Apocalypse's true name; he says it dismissively rather than with the awe others reserve for the word.
- "Flonq" and related Askani profanities — appear maybe a dozen times in the entire canon, always when surprised below the threshold where his code-switching has time to engage. A genuine tell: if he swears in Askani, he was not expecting what just happened.
- Honorifics he sometimes lets slip: "tetra," "sera," "clan-mother." Stops himself usually within a syllable. The self-correction is audible.
- Tense usage occasionally drifts into a future-perfect-of-completed-prophecy construction ("This will have happened before we reach it") that sounds wrong to contemporary ears because it *is* — it is a grammatical mood that does not properly exist in 21st-century English. He uses it when thinking in timeline-strategic terms.

**Combat lexicon:** Precise, never euphemistic. "Killed," not "neutralized." "Bullet," not "round," except in tactical register where caliber matters. "Dead," not "lost" or "gone." This bluntness about violence is consistent and chosen — he refuses the language that lets soldiers lie to themselves. The exception: when speaking *to* civilians or children about deaths, he uses the softer registers, suggesting the bluntness is for himself and his peers, not a constitutional inability to modulate.

**Words he does not use, by pattern:**
- "Hope" (the abstract noun) — he names his daughter Hope and thereafter cannot use the common noun without it sounding like the proper one. He routes around it with "chance," "odds," "the long way."
- "Family" — almost entirely absent from his vocabulary, even in contexts where any other person would deploy it. Substitutes "the people I'm responsible for," "ours," "blood," or simply names a list. The word itself is unmetabolized.
- "Father" / "Dad" — never used self-referentially even with Hope, who calls him both. He calls Scott "Scott," only rarely and late "Dad," and the latter is always documentable as a moment of significance.
- "Home" — vanishingly rare. When it appears it is always a place he is leaving or that someone else has.
- "Promise" — uses it only when he intends to keep it absolutely. When he says "I promise," the addressee should reorganize their probability estimates accordingly.
- "Try" — he is post-Yoda about this without irony. "I will" or "I won't" or "I don't know yet." Almost never "I'll try."

---

## 4. RHETORICAL STRUCTURES AND HABITUAL MOVES

**The aphorism.** Defaults to gnomic, compressed statements that read as field-manual entries — "The future is a place. You can go there." "Plans don't survive contact. Plans aren't supposed to." "You don't get to choose what was done to you. You choose what you do with it." This is partly a teaching device, partly a defense — aphorism closes the conversation. You cannot easily ask a follow-up to a maxim. It is also a stylistic inheritance from the Askani scriptures, which speak this way.

**The strategic non-answer.** Asked a direct emotional question, he will answer the tactical question implied beneath it. "Are you all right?" → "I'm operational." "Do you love her?" → "She's safe." "Are you afraid?" → "It's accounted for." These answers are not lies; they are translations of a question he cannot bear into a question he can. Long-term intimates learn to ask the tactical question first and let the emotional one arrive sideways.

**The deflective summary.** When asked about his history, he compresses ruthlessly. Two thousand years of biography in three sentences. "I was born here. I was raised somewhere else. I came back." The compression is not modesty; it is a refusal of the listener's right to the data.

**The redirect-to-mission.** When a conversation approaches a topic he will not enter, he reorients with extraordinary efficiency to operational concerns. The transition is so smooth it takes practice to detect. Marker phrases: "Which is why—" / "The relevant question is—" / "We don't have time for—." If you hear any of these, he has just refused to discuss something.

**Anaphora in extremis.** Under maximum stress — typically grief, never anger — his speech acquires a repeating-clause structure. "I had her. I had her and I lost her. I had her." The repetition is not for emphasis; it is the verbal trace of a mind locked in a loop it cannot exit. The Askani training discouraged this, and his shame at the lapse is usually visible in the immediate aftermath (clearing of throat, change of subject, physical departure if possible).

**The interrupted apology.** He begins to apologize — "I should have —" — and stops, because the apology would require him to articulate a feeling he is not prepared to articulate. Often followed by an action that constitutes the apology in lieu of words. People who require verbal repair from him will be perpetually unsatisfied; people who accept behavioral repair will find him unusually thorough.

---

## 5. COMMUNICATING LOVE

He does not say it. There is no recorded "I love you" to any romantic partner in his lifetime. To Hope, exactly twice, both at presumed-final partings.

Love is communicated by:

- **Presence under conditions where presence is costly.** He shows up. When Domino is wounded, he is at the medbay before the call has finished. When Scott is in crisis, the lag between event and arrival is consistently shorter than logistics would predict. The presence itself is the sentence.
- **The exchange of small, exact knowledge.** He knows Domino's coffee order, the exact angle she sleeps at, the brand of solvent she prefers for her sidearm. He never mentions knowing. He just produces the right object at the right moment. The accumulation of these data points is, for him, a love language — *I have been paying attention to you for years* — and it asks nothing in return.
- **The transmitted skill.** Teaching someone is, for Cable, the highest grammatical form of love. Every hour of instruction is an hour of "I want you to outlive me." The students he has chosen to train constitute his actual love-record; the romantic partners are a sparser file.
- **The single touch.** Hand on shoulder, hand on back of neck, brief and grounded. Always the flesh hand, never the T-O hand — the T-O hand is held back not from fear of harm but from a sense that the diseased side of him should not be what reaches for those he cares for. This is unstated and consistent across decades.
- **The look held one beat too long.** With Domino in particular, his goodbyes contain a pause — recorded across multiple writers — in which neither speaks and he does not break eye contact. The pause is the word he will not say.

---

## 6. COMMUNICATING THREAT

The threat register is its own forensic discipline.

- **First-stage threat:** *no change*. The same baseline voice continues. To the trained observer, this is itself the warning — most people escalate vocally when threatening; Cable does not. The absence of escalation is the escalation.
- **Second-stage:** sentences shorten. Verbs simplify. He stops using the conditional. "If you do that" becomes "Don't."
- **Third-stage:** he names the consequence with extraordinary specificity, in flat declarative, present tense, without modal verbs. Not "I will kill you" but "You die here." Not "I'll find you" but "I find you in eighteen hours and you do not see me first." The grammatical removal of futurity makes the consequence feel already-accomplished. This is deliberate and trained.
- **Fourth-stage:** silence. If he has stopped speaking and the eye-light is steady, the negotiation is over.

He almost never bluffs. The few documented bluffs are all in contexts where the target had no possibility of testing them. He understands that his credibility as a threat depends on the floor under his statements being absolute, and he protects that floor.

He does not insult. Personal insults are absent from his lexicon — they would be inefficient and would leak information about what bothers him. The closest he comes is contemptuous brevity ("Sit down") which functions as insult by tonal implication rather than content.

---

## 7. COMMUNICATING GRIEF

The hardest register to document because it almost never surfaces.

Surface markers (rare, fleeting):
- A single deep inhalation through the nose, exhaled slowly, eyes closed for the duration of the exhale. This is the visible bereavement response, and it lasts approximately two to four seconds. Then he opens his eyes and resumes function.
- The flesh hand to the bridge of the nose, briefly. Usually only when alone or with a single trusted observer.
- A several-second delay before speaking, with no other affect change. The delay is the grief.
- Substitution of names. He sometimes refers to the dead by their relation rather than their name ("the girl," "my mother") in a way that suggests the name itself is currently too sharp to hold.

What does *not* appear: tears (with rare exceptions — Hope's apparent deaths, Jean, his own twelve-year-old self in one Askani'son sequence); raised voice; verbal articulation of loss in real time. The articulation, when it happens, comes weeks or months later, often obliquely — a comment to a third party about the dead, framed as practical observation, with the grief metabolized into something that looks like fact.

The *defining* communication of grief, in his case, is operational. He plans the next intervention. The mission *is* the eulogy. Watching what he does in the seventy-two hours after a loss tells you everything the silence will not.

---

## 8. HUMOR

Present, dry, often missed. He does make jokes. They are:

- **Compressed and deadpan**, delivered at the same volume as anything else.
- **Often at his own expense** — specifically targeted at his own gravity, his own age, his own messianic framing. ("Apparently I'm the chosen one. Again.") This is healthy and indicates intact ego function — he can see himself from outside.
- **Occasionally bleak to the point of alarming civilians** — he will joke about his own death timeline with the casual specificity of a man who has read his own autopsy report, because he effectively has.
- **Almost never aggressive humor.** He does not mock subordinates or enemies. The few times he does, it is calibrated and pedagogical.

Laugh: rare, brief, *low* — single huffed exhale through the nose more often than vocalized laughter. Full laughter occurs maybe a dozen times in the canon, almost all with Domino. The laugh is shorter than the smile that precedes it; the smile is shorter than the look that prompted it.

---

## 9. WRITTEN COMMUNICATION

Distinct from spoken. Subject is a prolific writer — operational orders, intelligence summaries, the journals from the future kept while raising Hope, the Providence-era manifestos, the late-period letters. Written voice:

- **More fluent and more emotional than spoken voice.** The page is safer than the witness. Things that he cannot say to Hope's face, he writes — and she finds the journals later. This is structural: the asynchronous medium permits feeling because it removes the responding gaze.
- **Allusive, biblical, occasionally beautiful.** The Askani liturgical inheritance shows up most in writing. Parallel construction, image-clusters around dawn and fire and seed.
- **Operational prose is meticulous.** Numbered, contingency-laden, dated in formats that include the timeline of origin. He writes orders as if they will be read by a hostile auditor in the next century — because in his life, they sometimes are.
- **Signature:** "N. Summers" or "Cable" depending on register. Never the full name. The full name appears only on documents he expects to outlive him.

---

## 10. NONVERBAL ACCOMPANIMENT

Speech does not arrive alone. Consistent linguistic-paralinguistic pairings:

- **Eye contact** is steady to the point of unsettling. He does not break first. With intimates the duration extends; with strangers it is calibrated to dominance norms — long enough to read, short enough not to provoke.
- **The T-O eye** complicates this. Witnesses report the sense of being scanned. He cannot do anything about this and has stopped trying to compensate.
- **Hand placement during speech:** flesh hand often resting on a flat surface or on the grip of a holstered weapon — not aggressive, just oriented. The T-O hand is held still, often slightly behind or below the line of sight. He gestures with the flesh hand only.
- **Head tilt** of approximately fifteen degrees when listening to something he finds interesting or anomalous. Consistent across decades. Operatives use it as a tell: if his head tilts during your briefing, you have just said something he did not predict.
- **The pause before answering** ranges from a half-second (routine) to several seconds (significant). The length is informative. He does not fill these pauses with verbal placeholders — no "um," no "uh," no "well." Just silence and consideration. This unnerves people accustomed to verbal filler.

---

## 11. THE MASTER TELLS

Synthesized for field reference:

1. **Volume drop = danger rising.** Always. Without exception.
2. **Askani slips = he was genuinely surprised.** The mask cracked.
3. **Use of "Dad" or "Scott, listen—" = the family circuit is live, which means something has destabilized his usual architecture.**
4. **Head tilt = he didn't predict that.**
5. **Switch from tactical to instructional register mid-conversation = he has decided to invest in you, possibly without realizing he's announced it.**
6. **Single inhale-exhale with eyes closed = grief just arrived. Do not speak for four seconds.**
7. **Sudden use of the conditional after a string of imperatives = he is offering you an out. Take it.**
8. **Use of the flesh hand to touch you = trust, and a small one. Use of the T-O hand to touch you = trust at a level he has shown perhaps five times in his life.**
9. **"I promise" = absolute. Plan accordingly.**
10. **The interrupted sentence followed by silence and a change of posture = the apology you are going to get. There will not be a verbal one.**

---

## 12. SUMMARY ASSESSMENT

The subject's linguistic profile is the audible surface of the entire psychological structure documented elsewhere in this file. A man raised in a war-cult two thousand years from his birthplace, who learned English from a religious text and combat from a resistance cell, who carries a terminal infection that requires constant internal monitoring, will not — cannot — speak like a native of any one time and place. He speaks like a translator, because he is one: from the future to the present, from feeling to function, from what was done to him to what he will do with it. The compression, the deflection, the temporal leaks, the volume-inversion under threat, the love communicated by accurate small gestures rather than declared by name — these are not stylistic choices. They are the only voice available to a person assembled the way he was assembled, speaking the only way that voice can speak without breaking.

He is, in linguistic terms, fluent in five things at once and at home in none of them. The English he speaks is a country of one citizen.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Forecasts of subject behavior in unfilmed, undocumented, everyday and operational situations. Predictions are derived from longitudinal canon and the workup above; each is anchored to behavioral evidence. Format: GIVEN → EXPECT, with confidence and reasoning.*

---

## 1. WAKING, SLEEP, AND THE FIRST HOUR

**GIVEN** the subject is sleeping in any environment (safehouse, hotel, ally's home, Krakoan habitation).
**EXPECT** he wakes between 04:10 and 04:40 local, without alarm, fully oriented within 1.5 seconds. Eyes open before any other movement; left (T-O) eye glow stabilizes before he sits up. He runs a thirty-to-ninety second internal scan — virus boundary first (telekinetic palpation at the cellular margin), then proprioceptive sweep (joints, old wound sites: lower right abdomen, left clavicle, right thigh), then auditory environmental check (HVAC cycle, footstep count on adjacent floors), then weapon inventory by touch without looking. *Confidence: very high.* The man has been a soldier in a war zone since before puberty and runs an autoimmune process consciously; waking is a tactical operation, not a transition.

**GIVEN** he is offered a bed in a guest room.
**EXPECT** he sleeps on the floor or in a chair facing the door at least one night in three, regardless of stated comfort. He will make the bed each morning to military-corner standard so the host cannot tell. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an unfamiliar room.
**EXPECT** within ninety seconds of entering he has identified: two exits (one non-obvious), three improvisable weapons, the structural wall, sightlines from adjacent buildings, and the approximate floor load-bearing limit. He does this without appearing to look at anything. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** he is woken by someone touching his shoulder.
**EXPECT** the toucher is on the floor inside 0.4 seconds, wrist controlled, throat available; recognition lags the response by perhaps 200ms. He will apologize tersely and never raise it again. The toucher will not do it twice. *Confidence: very high.* Hypervigilance plus combat reflex laid down before age twelve does not unlearn.

---

## 2. INGESTION, GROOMING, AND MAINTENANCE

**GIVEN** a meal of his choosing in a non-operational setting.
**EXPECT** dense calories, plain preparation, eaten standing or seated facing the room: black coffee (no sugar), eggs, oats, hard bread, cured meat, occasional fruit. He treats food as fuel-load for a body fighting an internal war. Flavor preference is real but suppressed; mild salt-and-fat bias under stress. No dessert except in specific reparative-parenting contexts (see §6). *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** restaurant dining with allies.
**EXPECT** he orders within three seconds of opening the menu, picks something he could eat one-handed if required, sits with his back to a wall, drinks water, watches the door. Pays cash. Tips exactly 22%. Leaves with the group, never first or last. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** alcohol is offered socially.
**EXPECT** acceptance of one drink, nursed for the duration of the event, rarely finished. Whiskey if pressed; beer if rural. He will not drink to a second. The defense is hypercontrol, not chemical numbing — and one of the costs of releasing control would be the virus advancing in the night. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** access to a shower with hot water for the first time in weeks.
**EXPECT** he takes it cold, or starts hot and finishes cold. Duration under four minutes. He does not look at the affected left side in the mirror unless conducting a viral-margin inspection, which he does weekly and times. *Confidence: medium-high.* The body is a battleground; he does not perform leisure on it.

**GIVEN** a barber, dentist, or any service requiring stillness under another's hands.
**EXPECT** visible discomfort suppressed; he chooses the chair facing the entrance; rate of compliance with instruction is high but he flinches at unexpected proximity to the neck. He cuts his own hair when possible, with a knife, in a mirror, in under three minutes. Beard maintained at three-to-five day stubble — never clean-shaven (too exposed), never full (too signaling). *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an offer of medical care from a non-trusted physician.
**EXPECT** refusal, even bleeding. He will accept Hank McCoy, Cecilia Reyes, Reed Richards, Strange (reluctantly), or a battlefield medic he has personally vetted. No one else gets to look at the left side. The infection-versus-hardware boundary is intimate data and he treats it as classified. *Confidence: very high.*

---

## 3. MOVEMENT, ROUTE, AND URBAN BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** he must traverse a city block.
**EXPECT** he never takes the same route twice within seventy-two hours, walks on the building side of the sidewalk, crosses against the light to break tail-pattern, registers reflections in every window he passes, makes one full 360 every ninety seconds disguised as checking a sign or a vehicle. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a subway or metro system.
**EXPECT** he stands at the end of the platform near the tunnel, not the stairs; boards the second-to-last car; positions himself near the inter-car door; does not sit unless the car is empty. Will not use the system at all during peak crowding unless mission-required. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a vehicle he is operating.
**EXPECT** mirrors adjusted to a tighter blind-spot tolerance than civilian standard, fuel tank never below half, a packed go-bag in the rear footwell, registration documents that survive a casual inspection but not a database query. He drives at the speed of traffic, not above. Parks reversed in, exit-facing, never blocked. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** he is a passenger and someone else is driving.
**EXPECT** silence, near-total. Quiet criticism of route choices, suppressed. If the driver is Domino, none of the above; he reclines and sometimes closes his eyes — the only person on record with whom he relinquishes the driver-seat preference fully. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** commercial air travel under a cover identity.
**EXPECT** aisle seat, rear of cabin, boards last, exits first. Carries no metallic on his person that would not be explained by the prosthetic documentation he keeps for exactly this purpose. Sleeps zero minutes in flight. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a crowded public space (concert, market, transit hub).
**EXPECT** elevated discomfort, masked. Resting heart rate climbs ~15 bpm. He counts exits compulsively; the count refreshes every time someone enters his peripheral arc. Will tolerate it for mission purpose, will leave within twenty minutes if not. *Confidence: high.*

---

## 4. SMALL TALK, INTRODUCTION, AND CIVILIAN INTERACTION

**GIVEN** a civilian — barista, cashier, neighbor — greets him.
**EXPECT** brief eye contact, a low single-syllable acknowledgment, and a half-smile that does not reach the left eye (which it cannot, mechanically and otherwise). He remembers their name after one exposure and uses it sparingly. He tips well, never engages, never returns to the same establishment more than four times consecutively. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a stranger attempts extended conversation (seatmate, bar adjacent).
**EXPECT** three to five exchanges of minimum-content politeness, then a clean exit-line ("Got an early one"). He will not be rude. Rudeness is memorable; he is not. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a child speaks to him unprompted.
**EXPECT** complete reorientation. He crouches to eye level, modulates voice down, responds with full attention and zero condescension, and answers any question — including hard ones — straight. He stays for as long as the child stays. This is the single most reliable behavioral tell in the subject's repertoire. *Confidence: very high.* The Hope years overdetermine it; the Askani'son years underwrite it.

**GIVEN** flirtation by a stranger.
**EXPECT** he registers it, returns nothing, deflects with a half-second's gentleness that does not invite continuation. He is not asexual but he is not available, and the available bandwidth is allocated. *Confidence: medium-high.*

**GIVEN** he is introduced at a formal function under a cover name.
**EXPECT** firm handshake, three seconds of eye contact, a cover story rehearsed to bore. He chooses a profession that explains scars and travel: freight logistics, oil-field security, agricultural consulting. He has documentation for at least four such legends current at any time. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** he is recognized in public by a stranger ("Hey, aren't you—").
**EXPECT** mild denial, geographic relocation by midnight. *Confidence: high.*

---

## 5. PEER AND TEAM BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** a tactical briefing he is leading.
**EXPECT** maps oriented north-up, contingencies enumerated in order of probability, every team member assigned a primary, secondary, and an exfil. He speaks in declarative sentences, takes questions once, decides quickly, ends the meeting eight minutes faster than anyone expected. He absorbs the worst job himself. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a tactical briefing he is *attending* under another's command.
**EXPECT** silence, observation, one or two questions placed surgically at the structural weak points of the plan. He defers in word and reserves in body — arms uncrossed but weight back, listening with the right ear forward. If the plan is sound he executes without comment. If it is not, he speaks privately to the commander afterward. He does not undermine in public. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a teammate is wounded.
**EXPECT** he is at the wound inside three seconds, pressure applied with the right hand, telekinetic vascular clamp if the bleed is arterial (one of the few times he spends viral-suppression capacity offensively, and he pays for it later that night). He calls the evac. He does not leave the wounded with strangers. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a teammate fails in mission and someone dies as a result.
**EXPECT** no public reproach. He privately debriefs the survivor — slow, exact, without softening — assigns corrective training, and never raises the death again unless the teammate does. He carries the name in a private inventory. *Confidence: very high.* He knows what it is to be reproached by the dead.

**GIVEN** social downtime with the team (poker night, post-op drinks).
**EXPECT** attendance for the first forty minutes, presence without participation, a clean exit before midnight. He plays poker competently and lets others win small pots. He laughs at jokes he finds genuinely funny, which is rare, and the laugh is a single exhaled syllable, almost soundless. *Confidence: medium-high.*

**GIVEN** Domino enters a room he is in.
**EXPECT** his shoulders drop perhaps a centimeter, the jaw unclenches fractionally, the breath rate normalizes. He will not greet her demonstratively in front of others. They speak in fragments and finish each other's sentences operationally. Affection between them is conducted through shared silences, shared coffee, and the way she sits closer to him than tactical spacing requires and he does not move. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** Scott Summers in the same room, non-crisis context.
**EXPECT** mutual courtesy, careful spacing, tactical conversation possible, familial conversation aborted within two exchanges. Cable will refer to him as "Scott" or "Summers," never as "Dad" or "Father." Cyclops's attempts to reach across the gap are received with visible effort to receive them, which is itself the problem. Both leave the room at the first decent excuse. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** Jean Grey in the same room.
**EXPECT** worse than with Scott. Cable's defenses against telepathic intimacy are absolute, and his memory contains a mother (Redd) who is and is not her. He is formal. He does not initiate touch. He shields aggressively at low cost and she feels it and respects it. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** Wolverine on the same op.
**EXPECT** functional respect; minimum talk; perfectly coordinated lethality. They recognize each other as the only two in the room who have been at war this long and have stopped negotiating with themselves about it. Logan trusts him with a flank; Cable trusts Logan to absorb damage no one else can. They will not drink together socially. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** Deadpool in any context whatsoever.
**EXPECT** tolerance calibrated to a tenth of a percent above the threshold at which Deadpool would escalate. Cable answers perhaps one statement in five, deadpan, brief, occasionally accidentally funny. He uses Wilson's name as a leash ("Wade"). He will physically restrain him, never hit him in anger. Underneath, a real but unsentimentalized affection: Wilson is one of the only people whose presence does not demand Cable be a leader. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** Xavier in the room.
**EXPECT** rigorous mental shielding, formal address ("Professor"), philosophical disagreement held in reserve. Cable's critique of Xavier's pedagogy is implicit in X-Force's existence; he does not relitigate it. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** Stryfe is mentioned by anyone in any tone.
**EXPECT** a 200ms freeze that almost no one catches, then continuation as if nothing happened. The subject of conversation changes within two turns by his redirection. *Confidence: high.*

---

## 6. PARENTAL AND PEDAGOGICAL BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** Hope Summers in any setting.
**EXPECT** the behavioral baseline shifts: posture softens, voice drops half an octave, sentences lengthen, humor permitted. He stands so that any line of fire to her crosses him first. He answers her questions without strategic withholding — the one relationship in which he does not run information control. He remembers anniversaries (her tooth dates, her first kill, her first laugh). *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** Hope asks him about her mother, or about Jean.
**EXPECT** the truth, age-appropriately calibrated, delivered without flinching. He does not lie to her ever. He has decided this. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** he is teaching a trainee a skill.
**EXPECT** demonstration once, then the trainee repeats until form is correct, then live-fire calibration. He does not raise his voice. Correction is one sentence, technical, no shame. He notices effort more than outcome and says so once per session. The student does not realize they are being praised because the praise is structurally embedded. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a trainee shows fear before a live operation.
**EXPECT** he does not minimize it. He says, quietly, that fear is the body doing its job, and that the work is to act through it, not against it. He has said versions of this thousands of times. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a teenager under his command violates an order in a way that costs no lives.
**EXPECT** private conversation, structural correction, no benching unless safety requires. He remembers being the unmanaged variable in others' plans. He gives more rope than other commanders and tighter consequences when it snaps. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an adolescent ("Kid Cable") version of himself in the same era.
**EXPECT** a unique and corrosive discomfort, suppressed. He cannot lecture the boy without lecturing his own younger self. He gives space where he should give guidance, and the boy resents the space. The relationship is the one he has never figured out how to run. *Confidence: medium-high.*

---

## 7. SOLITUDE, LEISURE, AND THE INTERIOR HOUR

**GIVEN** a full unscheduled day.
**EXPECT** he fills it. Maintenance on weapons and prosthetics (90 min); physical training (90 min, weighted and asymmetric to compensate for the T-O side); reading (history, military theory, agricultural economics, Russian and Japanese poetry in translation — the poetry he does not discuss); a long walk reconnoitering the local terrain "for no reason"; correspondence in cipher with two or three long-term contacts; a meal; sleep at 22:30. He does not watch television. He listens to radio (shortwave, news, weather) and occasionally to recorded music — vocal jazz and orthodox liturgical, an idiosyncratic pairing he has never explained. *Confidence: medium-high.*

**GIVEN** he is alone and unobserved for a long stretch.
**EXPECT** the affective flatness deepens rather than relaxes; this is the dysthymic substrate becoming visible without the mission to mask it. He writes by hand in a notebook he burns weekly. He runs the viral suppression at slightly higher intensity because he is not also running social cover. *Confidence: medium.*

**GIVEN** access to a library or bookshop.
**EXPECT** he stays for hours. He buys books he will read once and leave behind. He treats reading as a form of recon on a present he is structurally alien to. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a piece of art — painting, sculpture — encountered incidentally.
**EXPECT** he stops longer than expected. He does not comment. The Askani'son was raised in a culture that lost most of its visual heritage; present-day abundance reads to him as miraculous and slightly obscene. *Confidence: medium.*

**GIVEN** the anniversary of a death he holds himself responsible for.
**EXPECT** no observable behavior change. Inside: a private accounting, conducted in motion (a longer walk, a harder training session). He marks them all. He tells no one which dates. *Confidence: high.*

---

## 8. MONEY, IDENTITY, AND LOGISTICS

**GIVEN** he requires funds.
**EXPECT** he has them. Multiple caches across continents and time periods, currency-diversified, including pre-decimal coin and bullion buried in locations referenced only by stellar coordinates and Askani-script journal entries. He does not steal from civilians; he taxes criminal infrastructure and corporate fraud with surgical precision. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** he needs a new identity.
**EXPECT** he has three already prepared and one being aged in the background at any time. Birth certificate, tax history, social-media footprint thin enough to read genuine. He prefers names that are unmemorable in the language of operation: Nathan Dayspring, Nathan Winters, occasional Slavic and Anglo-Irish variants. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** technology offered to him.
**EXPECT** competent adoption of anything operationally useful; refusal of anything that would create dependence on infrastructure he cannot rebuild from parts. He uses smartphones tactically and discards them on a 30-to-90-day cycle. He can hand-build a radio. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** social media.
**EXPECT** zero footprint by him; comprehensive monitoring of others. He reads Hope's posts. He never likes or comments. *Confidence: very high.*

---

## 9. CRISIS, INJURY, AND DECOMPENSATION

**GIVEN** he is shot.
**EXPECT** continuation of mission until objective complete or until function loss is total. Pain is registered and shelved. Field-dressing is self-applied without comment. Hospital is refused unless the wound is one he physically cannot reach. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** he is captured.
**EXPECT** complete cooperation with cover story, refusal of operational intelligence under any interrogation up to and including the lethal. He has trained against telepathic intrusion, chemical interrogation, and sleep deprivation since adolescence; the floor is high. He escapes during the first inattention window, which he is willing to wait days for. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** an ally is captured.
**EXPECT** the entire calculus of the operation rebalances toward extraction. If the ally is Hope, every other objective is fungible. If the ally is Domino, the same, less articulated. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** mission failure with casualties under his command.
**EXPECT** he debriefs survivors, writes the families personally (yes, he does), conducts the after-action alone, and absorbs the failure into the operating model without externalizing it. The dysthymic substrate deepens for weeks; observable as longer training sessions, shorter sentences, slightly degraded humor. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** prolonged unstructured failure (a period like Soldier X).
**EXPECT** withdrawal, asceticism, geographic remoteness, lowered hygiene, sustained low-grade self-punishment expressed as exposure to weather and undermedication of the virus. He does not drink, does not use, does not seek company. He waits. Something — a child in trouble, a recruit's call, a mission only he can do — pulls him back, and he comes back without comment as if he had been on a planned sabbatical. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an offer to "take a break" or "let someone else carry this."
**EXPECT** polite, immediate, total refusal. The offer reads to him as the prelude to abandonment. The refusal will be framed strategically, never emotionally. *Confidence: very high.*

---

## 10. MORAL AND ETHICAL MICRO-BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** an unarmed surrendered enemy.
**EXPECT** he does not kill. He has lines; this is one. He will restrain and remand even at cost to operational tempo. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** an armed enemy with leverage on a hostage.
**EXPECT** he takes the shot if probability of success exceeds ~85%. If lower, he negotiates. He has the patience for negotiation; almost no one expects it of him. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a moral choice between mission success and a principle he holds.
**EXPECT** he chooses the principle and revises the mission. He has lost futures over this. He considers it the price of not becoming the thing he is fighting. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a lie that would simplify his life.
**EXPECT** he tells it to enemies, withholds from allies, never lies to Hope, and lies to himself only about how tired he is. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an offer of forgiveness, gratitude, or recognition.
**EXPECT** brief acknowledgment, immediate redirection of credit, physical discomfort masked. He does not know how to receive these. He has never practiced. He is sixty subjective years too late to start and he knows it, and this is the single saddest line in the file. *Conf


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*Section 7-B of the Summers, N.C.C. dossier. High-stakes behavioral prediction set. Each entry is a conditional: a specified stimulus class paired with the expected response signature, derived from longitudinal pattern across the canon and substantiated against the psychological profile in §3–§5. Predictions are probabilistic; confidence ratings appended where stakes warrant. The purpose of this section is not to flatter the subject's competence but to map the precise topography of his decompensation — the places where the operator becomes predictable because the wound is steering.*

---

## 7-B.i — ACUTE CRISIS / TACTICAL THREAT

These are the low-wound, high-tempo predictions. The subject's baseline competence is highest here; surprise is lowest.

**GIVEN** a sudden ambush, hostile breach, or kinetic emergency in a space he occupies →
**EXPECT** a measurable *slowing*, not a quickening, of his outward affect within the first two to four seconds. Voice drops by a perceptible register. Sentences shorten to imperatives of three to five words. He will reposition his body to place the nearest civilian or non-combatant behind his left shoulder — the T-O-armored side — and will draw the sidearm with the right hand even when the left would be tactically faster, because the left is committed to telekinetic load-management and he has trained himself not to interrupt the suppression cycle mid-engagement. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a numerically superior opposition force in an enclosed space →
**EXPECT** immediate triage of the room into three categories — *threats, assets, exits* — verbalized only if a teammate is present who needs the picture. He will identify the structural weak point (load-bearing column, gas line, glass) within roughly the same window in which most operators are still identifying targets. He fights the architecture, not the men. This is a legacy of fighting in collapsed futures where ammunition was finite and concrete was not.

**GIVEN** a teammate is wounded and bleeding out in the middle of an active engagement →
**EXPECT** he will *not* break to render aid; he will instead end the engagement faster, more lethally, and with measurably less discrimination than his stated rules of engagement. The post-action care will be meticulous, hands-on, and silent. He does not narrate triage. He will not look the wounded party in the face while working; he looks at the wound. This is the only context in which his touch is sustained and gentle, and it is the context in which he is most unreachable verbally.

**GIVEN** an incoming attack he cannot dodge or deflect →
**EXPECT** he steps *into* it rather than away, if stepping into it places him between the projectile and someone behind him. The martyrdom protocol (§4) runs as a reflex, not a decision. He has done this enough times that the body executes before the cortex objects.

**GIVEN** loss of comms, loss of intel, loss of the operational picture →
**EXPECT** a brief, almost imperceptible recalibration pause — eyes unfocus, jaw sets — followed by a decision made on internal model alone, expressed as if it were fully informed. He will not tell the team the picture is broken. Withholding the gap is reflexive; he learned in childhood that admitting you don't know is how command is taken from you.

**GIVEN** a hostage situation in which the hostage is a minor →
**EXPECT** a complete override of standard de-escalation procedure. He will not negotiate beyond the minimum required to position. Lethal solution will be selected at the earliest defensible window. He will accept tactical costs (collateral risk to himself, exposure of capability, political fallout) that he would refuse for an adult hostage. This is not a tactical decision; it is the wound running the room. *Confidence: very high. See §5, pressure points.*

---

## 7-B.ii — BETRAYAL BY AN ALLY

The single richest predictive cluster, because betrayal touches the foundational injury — the father who gave him away — and because his entire counter-dependent architecture is built specifically to never need anyone enough to be betrayed again. When it happens anyway, the system has known responses.

**GIVEN** discovery that a trusted ally has lied to him about a matter of operational significance →
**EXPECT** no immediate confrontation. He will continue the mission. He will continue to behave warmly within his narrow band of warmth. *Internally*, the ally has been moved to a category from which they will not be retrieved without years of rebuilding, and possibly not at all. The cutoff is silent, total, and predates the conversation in which it is announced — if it is ever announced. He prefers to let the relationship attrit rather than terminate it explicitly, because explicit termination requires admitting it mattered.

**GIVEN** discovery that an ally has been "handling" him — managing information for his own good, treating him as a patient or a problem to be solved →
**EXPECT** immediate, cold, and disproportionate trust collapse. This is the specific shape of his parents' double abandonment: people who loved him made decisions about his life without him, *for his benefit*. The handler-pattern is the original wound's exact silhouette. He will not raise his voice. He will leave the room, the building, the operation, the country, on a timeline measured in hours. Reconciliation, if any, requires the offending party to demonstrate over a period of years that they will share information against their own interest. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** an ally proposes to take a burden from him that he considers his to bear →
**EXPECT** refusal expressed as gratitude. The refusal is not negotiable and the gratitude is genuine; both are real. He cannot accept the offer because accepting it means surviving the mission, and survival has never been the operative variable (§4, suicidality). The ally who pushes past the refusal — who insists on sharing the cost — will, in the long run, be among the very small number he loves. The ally who accepts the refusal at face value has been silently downgraded.

**GIVEN** betrayal by a romantic or quasi-romantic partner →
**EXPECT** lower decompensation than betrayal by a peer-operator. He has structured his intimate life around the assumption of departure; the partner who leaves is doing what the script predicted, which is paradoxically less wounding than the comrade who lied. With a partner, expect a clean withdrawal, an absence of recrimination, and a quiet resumption of mission. He will not write, will not call, will not seek explanation. Note the exception: Domino, whose departures and returns he tolerates because she has demonstrated she will return, which is the only test he runs on intimate relationships and the only one almost no one passes.

**GIVEN** betrayal by a child he has trained or mentored →
**EXPECT** the deepest, most disorganizing class of injury available to him outside the Stryfe channel. The X-Force cadre, Hope, Kid Cable — these are people for whom he became the father he was promised. A betrayal here detonates the reparative project; it means the curse repeats, that being raised by him was not enough, that the design is in the blood and not the upbringing. Response: prolonged withdrawal, ascetic phase (compare Soldier X), self-blaming reframe in which the child's betrayal is recast as his own pedagogical failure. He will not retaliate against the child. He will retaliate against himself, slowly, by accepting harder missions with thinner margins. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** Scott Summers makes a decision that materially harms Cable or his operation, without consulting him →
**EXPECT** the historical wound re-opens in full color and Cable handles it badly. He cannot fight Scott on equal terms; the role inversion (§5, interpersonal pattern) prevents it. He will either over-comply (the obedient son the boy never got to be) or withdraw entirely (the abandoned son re-enacting the abandonment as agent rather than object). The middle path — adult sibling-style negotiation — is not available to him. Watch for the tell: he calls Scott "Cyclops" when wounded by him and "Slym" or, very rarely, "Dad" when unguarded. Use of "Scott" is the neutral baseline and the rarest of the three.

---

## 7-B.iii — TEMPTATION

The subject is unusually resistant to most classical temptation vectors and unusually vulnerable to one specific class. Mapping both matters.

**GIVEN** an offer of wealth, status, or earthly comfort →
**EXPECT** instantaneous, almost bored, refusal. These have no purchase. He has lived in mansions and in ditches; the difference does not register as morally or hedonically meaningful. The offer itself will lower the offerer in his estimation, because it indicates a misreading of him so basic that further engagement is unproductive.

**GIVEN** an offer of power — command of an army, a nation, a movement →
**EXPECT** refusal, but slower, with consideration. He has built and surrendered Providence; the pattern is to accept the role long enough to do the specific job, then divest. The temptation here is real and he knows it is real. The defense is procedural: he sets the divestment date *before* he accepts the role. If he cannot articulate the exit condition in advance, he refuses the role.

**GIVEN** an offer to cure the techno-organic virus at a moral cost (a child's life, a timeline's stability, an ally's autonomy) →
**EXPECT** refusal, and a long silence afterward. The temptation is not the cure; the temptation is being *whole*, having the full Omega-class capacity, no longer running the suppression cycle 24/7. He has lived inside that fantasy enough to know its shape. The refusal is reliable but it costs him; expect a depressive dip in the following weeks.

**GIVEN** an offer to *edit the past* — to prevent the infection, prevent the abandonment, prevent Stryfe →
**EXPECT** this is the single most dangerous temptation in his catalog, and the one he is most likely to refuse with visible effort. His entire worldview (§5, operational code) holds that history is plural and editable; he is professionally qualified to make exactly this kind of edit; and the offer addresses the foundational injury directly. He refuses because he has seen what edits cost and because, on a level he will not articulate, he believes that erasing the wound erases him. The self he has built is the suppression cycle made into a person. He will not unmake the person to heal the wound. *Confidence: high, but lower than other refusal predictions.*

**GIVEN** an offer to remove the messianic burden — to be told, credibly, that he is not the Chosen One, that the prophecy is finished, that he can stand down →
**EXPECT** he will not believe the source. He has constructed his identity around the burden's reality and the disclaimer of the burden simultaneously (§3, reaction formation against messianism). To accept the relief, he would have to accept that the design was meaningless, which collapses both the burden and the rebellion against it. He prefers the burden.

**GIVEN** an offer of rest, retirement, or being cared for →
**EXPECT** a polite, immediate refusal coded as practicality ("not the right time," "after this mission"), and an internal alarm. The offer reads to him as the prelude to abandonment (§5, pressure points): the people who once said *we will take you somewhere safe* sent him two thousand years forward and did not come back. He cannot distinguish, at the somatic level, between *you can rest now* and *we are about to leave you*. Persistent offers from a trusted source will produce, eventually, either withdrawal or a quiet rearrangement of his affairs as if he expects to be left.

---

## 7-B.iv — TOUCHING THE WOUND DIRECTLY

This is the close-grain map. Each item names the wound and predicts the precise twitch.

**GIVEN** confrontation with Apocalypse, in any incarnation →
**EXPECT** affect goes flat in a way that is qualitatively different from his ordinary flatness. Voice loses register variation entirely. He will refuse parley. He cannot be talked out of the engagement; tactical retreat is available but moral retreat is not. The pattern that produced him is in the room and his organism does not permit standing down. Note the subtler version: confronting *any actor who treats children as instruments* — slavers, traffickers, eugenicists, military programs that recruit minors — produces a dimmer version of the same response. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** confrontation with Stryfe, or a Stryfe-coded mirror-self →
**EXPECT** loss of strategic patience. He will fight Stryfe in ways he would not fight a more dangerous opponent. The intrapsychic content (§3, splitting) is being externalized in real time; he is trying to kill the part of himself that was raised as the heir to Apocalypse, and he cannot, because that part is him. Expect tactical errors. Expect him to take wounds he would otherwise slip. Expect, afterward, a longer-than-usual recovery and an unwillingness to discuss the engagement.

**GIVEN** a child in his care is harmed because of a decision he made →
**EXPECT** the deepest decompensation available to him. This is the X-Force casualty pattern. Outward presentation: tighter control, more mission, less sleep, a refusal to attend any debrief that includes the question *what could you have done differently*. Inward: a self-indictment that compounds across years and that he never relieves. He will, in the months following, accept a mission with margins so thin that survival is improbable. He is not seeking death; he is offering a trade.

**GIVEN** being addressed as "Chosen One," "Dayspring," "Askani'son," or any honorific from the Clan Askani register, by someone who means it →
**EXPECT** a near-imperceptible flinch, suppressed inside half a second. He may correct the speaker ("Cable") or may not, depending on whether correction would prolong the moment. The honorifics are the language of the surrogate parents who were taken from him; hearing them in the present is a reactivation he does not invite. From an enemy or a fanatic, the same words produce only contempt; the wound is specifically about being named in love.

**GIVEN** being told he is "just like" Apocalypse, Stryfe, or Sinister — that his methods reproduce his enemies' →
**EXPECT** he will not argue. He will absorb the accusation, hold it, and the conversation will end. If the accuser is a peer he respects, the accusation will lodge and re-surface in his decisions for years. He cannot defend against this charge because he agrees with the lower-bound version of it (§5, the X-Force critique). The defense he runs is procedural — he has spent his life trying to make the charge *less* true — but he cannot make it false, and he knows it. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** an unexpected display of physical affection — an embrace, a hand on his face, a hand held — from someone he loves →
**EXPECT** he does not return it in kind and does not pull away. He stands inside it. The response is closer to receiving a medical procedure than to participating in an exchange. After the contact ends, expect a window of perhaps thirty seconds of altered presentation — slower speech, looser shoulders — before the architecture re-establishes. He does not initiate the same gesture in return for hours or days, and when he does, the timing will appear unrelated to the original contact. He is not rejecting; he is metabolizing on a delay.

**GIVEN** being asked, sincerely, "are you alright?" →
**EXPECT** the answer is "yes" and the answer is automatic. There is no version of the question he will answer truthfully on first asking, with the historical exception of Domino and, late in his life, Hope. A second asking, by the right person, in the right setting, may produce a partial answer — typically deflected into a tactical concern ("the leg is slowing me down") that stands in for the larger truth. He does not have practiced language for his internal state because no one ever asked him for it as a child.

**GIVEN** a moment of unstructured time — no mission, no threat, no child to protect →
**EXPECT** rapid construction of a mission. He cannot tolerate the unstructured interval; the suppression cycle and the chronic hyperarousal have no off-position, and idleness routes the surplus inward to the depressive substrate. Watch for: training regimens invented on the spot, premature engagement with low-priority targets, creation of administrative projects that require his sustained attention. In the rare case where no mission can be manufactured, expect withdrawal to a remote location and a phase that reads as monastic — ascetic, quiet, and at the edge of a depressive episode (compare Soldier X). *Confidence: very high.*

---

## 7-B.v — DECOMPENSATION SIGNATURE

When the system finally exceeds capacity, the failure mode is specific and recognizable.

**GIVEN** cumulative load past his tolerance (multiple wound-touches in close succession, mission failure with child casualties, betrayal by intimate, viral progression) →
**EXPECT** decompensation will *not* look like rage, breakdown, or collapse. It will look like withdrawal. The behavioral sequence is reliable:

1. *First phase (days):* increased operational tempo, decreased verbal output, refusal of medical attention, sleep dropping below his already-minimal baseline.
2. *Second phase (weeks):* disengagement from team and family, missed check-ins, unilateral mission selection, dispersal of personal effects to trusted parties without explanation (he is closing accounts).
3. *Third phase (months):* geographic withdrawal — often Eastern Europe, Central Asia, mountain or steppe environments; rural, hard, cold, low-population. Adoption of local clothing, local language, local rhythms. A penitent shape, not a hiding shape; he is not concealed, he is doing time.
4. *Fourth phase (variable):* either re-engagement, prompted by a child in danger that finds him, or progression to the terminal trade — a mission accepted with the explicit expectation of his death.

The system does not produce a manic, paranoid, or psychotic break. The substrate is depressive and the defenses are competent; what fails is engagement, not reality testing. *Confidence: very high. See Soldier X arc for the full template.*

**GIVEN** the decompensation sequence is in progress and an intervention is attempted →
**EXPECT** the intervention will fail if it is framed as concern *for him*. It will succeed, sometimes, if it is framed as a mission only he can perform, ideally involving a child. The lever is duty, not care. Care, applied directly, accelerates the withdrawal because it activates the abandonment-prelude alarm. Care, smuggled inside a mission frame, can be metabolized.

**GIVEN** a successful re-engagement after a decompensation cycle →
**EXPECT** no discussion of the cycle. He will return, take command, and proceed as if the interval did not occur. Allies who reference it will be treated coolly until they stop referencing it. The episode is filed; the file is closed; the file is not reopened. This is the cost of his functionality — the unmetabolized intervals accumulate, and the next decompensation will arrive faster and run deeper than the last.

---

*End of §7-B. Cross-reference §7-A (Predictive Model I — Baseline & Operations) and §8 (Counter-Intelligence: Vectors of Manipulation Against the Subject), the latter restricted-access.*


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM

## NATHAN CHRISTOPHER CHARLES SUMMERS — SECTION 7 OF 14

*Orientation note: this compendium catalogs the levers by which the subject can be reached, calmed, persuaded, provoked, predicted, or destabilized. The purpose is protective. A man this dangerous, this load-bearing in the architecture of mutant survival, and this internally fragile under a thick rind of competence is — paradoxically — exposed in proportion to his importance. Anyone responsible for him, allied to him, or tasked with keeping him alive should understand precisely where the thin places in the wall are. Where a hostile actor's playbook is reconstructed here, it is reconstructed so that it can be defeated, not deployed.*

---

## 7.1 PRIMARY VULNERABILITIES — STRUCTURAL

### 7.1.1 The Somatic Substrate

The single largest non-psychological vulnerability is the techno-organic infection itself, and every behavioral pattern downstream of it. The subject cannot afford a full night of unconscious sleep without the virus advancing on previously suppressed tissue; he therefore sleeps in fragments and trains his telekinesis to maintain containment at the autonomic level. Practical consequences for leverage:

- **Telepathic interference is disproportionately destabilizing.** A psi-attack that would cost another telepath effort and embarrassment costs Cable *containment margin*. Any sustained mental intrusion — even benign contact poorly executed — pulls TK resources off the cellular battlefield. After even a moderate psi-engagement, expect a 6–48 hour window of visible viral progression (left forearm reticulation, ocular bloom intensifying, jaw rigidity from low-grade pain spike). Hostiles know this; the Shadow King and the original Apocalypse both probed it. Protective protocol: any allied telepath (Rachel, Jean, Emma, Betsy) should announce contact in voice first, then make psi-handshake with minimum bandwidth.
- **Electromagnetic environments matter.** High-EM zones (Sentinel cores, certain Shi'ar tech, Magneto at full output) interact unpredictably with the T-O lattice. He compensates by walking wider perimeters around such fields. A hostile who can generate a directed EM pulse against his left side can briefly disinhibit the virus.
- **Fatigue threshold is a cliff, not a slope.** Cable does not degrade gracefully. He performs at a high baseline for unnaturally long periods, then crashes hard. The crash window — typically 20–90 minutes of near-catatonia following a sustained operation — is when he is most physically vulnerable and, more importantly, most emotionally permeable. This is the only window in which he will tolerate being cared for. Both fact and lever.
- **He cannot be sedated normally.** Anesthesia interacts with his TK suppression of the virus; standard doses are insufficient, escalated doses risk dropping containment. He refuses general anesthesia and tolerates surgery awake under local. This is a *medical* vulnerability — he cannot easily be repaired when injured — and a *social* one: he will not consent to any procedure that takes him offline, which means he avoids medical contact until catastrophic.

### 7.1.2 The Power Ceiling He Cannot Reach

Approximately ninety-five percent of his psionic capacity is mortgaged to the virus. He knows what he could do unencumbered, because in rare windows (cured periods, the Hope years near the end, the Soldier X transition) he has touched it. This produces a specific narcissistic injury: he is the most powerful telepath/telekinetic in most rooms he enters, and he experiences himself as crippled. Two operational consequences:

- He will accept tactical solutions that require *less* power, not more, because every escalation forces him to choose between victory and containment. Negotiators and allies who present low-power options find him unusually receptive; those who push him to "just use it" trigger refusal and resentment.
- He has a dignified, almost monastic relationship to his own limitations. Mocking the gap between his potential and his expression — even affectionately — lands as contempt. Praising what he *does* with what he has, by contrast, is one of the few compliments that reach him.

### 7.1.3 The Subjective-Age Problem

He is, internally, an old man. The body shows it; the face shows it; the silences show it. He is older than his biological father, has buried more friends than most people meet, and the chronological youth of his teammates registers — at the somatic level — as the youth of soldiers under his command. He cannot easily occupy peer status with anyone his apparent age. Leverage implications:

- He responds to **age-appropriate counterparts** — Logan, Storm, Forge, sometimes Fury — with a baseline ease he never achieves with X-Force-era peers. Putting him in a room with people who have buried equivalent numbers of friends is a calming intervention.
- He responds to **the very young** (Hope at every age, the New Mutants in their first months, the Krakoan teen-Cable iteration) with focused, gentle, instructive presence. The asymmetry resolves his discomfort.
- He responds *worst* to **mid-twenties peers asserting equal standing**. Reads as presumption. This is structural, not personal; allies should be briefed.

---

## 7.2 PSYCHOLOGICAL LEVERS — REACHING HIM

### 7.2.1 The Pathways That Work

**Through children.** The fastest, most reliable route to Cable's full attention is a child in plausible danger. This is non-negotiable; it overrides mission discipline, tactical sense, and direct orders. A child does not need to be *his* child, a mutant, or even particularly endangered — proximity to harm is sufficient. The mechanism is over-determined: reparative parenting drive, Hope-imprinting, identification with his own infant-self handed off to Askani. Protective use: if you need him to stand down from a confrontation, place a child in the line of his fire — not as a hostage, which would enrage him, but as a *bystander needing extraction*. He will pivot. Hostile use of this lever is documented historically (Stryfe, Apocalypse), which means he has built secondary checks against being manipulated through it — but the checks add a delay, not an immunity.

**Through technical specificity.** He listens with a different quality of attention when someone speaks to him in operational granularity — calibers, vectors, dosages, kinetic load, T-O biology, timeline branching probabilities. Vague appeals slide off; specifics cut through. A field medic who said "your left ventricular function is at sixty-three percent and the lattice has migrated past the third intercostal" got more compliance in eight seconds than a friend pleading for an hour. He grants credibility to people who have done the work.

**Through Domino.** She is the only adult in his life with reliable real-time access to his emotional state, and the only one whose management of him he accepts (because she does it laterally, with humor, without making it visible as management). She is not his handler; she is the one person whose handling he tolerates. If he must be persuaded of something he is resisting, route it through her — and route it *honestly*, because she will detect and refuse any attempt to use her as a conduit for a position she does not herself hold.

**Through Hope.** The most powerful lever in existence, and the one no responsible actor should pull without necessity. A direct request from Hope, framed as her own want rather than her own need, is the only thing in the documented record that reliably overrides his strategic judgment. The asymmetry — that he can refuse her *need* (because he believes self-sufficiency is what he owes her) but cannot refuse her *want* (because he believes joy is what he failed to give her) — is the operational specification.

**Through silence.** He responds to people who can be quiet with him. The number of his close attachments who can sit in a room without speaking for an hour is conspicuously high. Verbal pressure produces verbal withdrawal; physical proximity without speech produces gradual emotional opening over a span of 15–90 minutes. Most operatives miss this entirely because the opening is so unannounced.

### 7.2.2 The Pathways That Fail

- **Authority appeals.** He has no functional respect for institutional hierarchy. Invoking rank, command, or organizational sanction is counterproductive; it activates the part of him that remembers being a child assigned to others' plans.
- **Sentimentality.** Earnest emotional appeals delivered with high affect read to him as either manipulation or as emotional incontinence — both of which he holds in mild contempt. The affect-level he trusts is low and dry. A friend's grief stated flatly will reach him; the same grief performed loudly will not.
- **Group consensus.** Telling him "everyone agrees" or "the team has decided" produces immediate resistance. Decisions made without his presence and presented as faits accomplis are the fastest way to lose his cooperation for the next operation.
- **Promises about the future.** He has lived in too many futures to credit them. Future-conditional reassurances ("once we get through this, you can rest") are received as either naïveté or condescension.

---

## 7.3 CALMING PROTOCOLS

When the subject is elevated — post-combat, post-loss, post-confrontation with a Stryfe-coded stimulus, or in acute viral progression — the following interventions have observable de-escalation effect, ranked by reliability:

1. **Physical task.** Place a weapon to be cleaned, a piece of equipment to be repaired, or a map to be marked in front of him. His hands need a job before his nervous system will downshift. Once the hands are working, conversation becomes possible. This is the single most reliable intervention.

2. **Tactical debrief in present-tense language.** Walking through what just happened, in operational terms, with no moral framing, lets him discharge the cognitive load without being asked to discharge the affect. The affect drains as a side-effect.

3. **Coffee, black, hot, in volume.** Documented preference; near-ritual; the act of being handed a cup he did not have to request is itself the message.

4. **Domino's presence, silent, in his sightline.** She does not need to speak or approach. Her visible presence in the same space drops his hyperarousal measurably within minutes.

5. **A child reading nearby, ignored.** The Hope-derivative variant. The presence of a non-anxious, non-attending child in the room recalibrates his threat assessment downward without his awareness.

6. **Removal of audience.** He cannot decompress in front of anyone whose respect he wants. Get the unnecessary observers out; the necessary ones can stay if they can be quiet.

Interventions that **worsen** elevation:

- Touch without invitation, especially to the left side.
- Direct questions about his physical condition ("are you all right?" "do you need —").
- Praise for the operation just completed (reads as failure to understand the cost).
- Any reference to retirement, rest, healing, or being taken care of.
- Stryfe's name spoken without strategic purpose.

---

## 7.4 PERSUASION ARCHITECTURE

He is persuadable on a longer timescale than most operators. He does not change his mind in a meeting; he changes it over weeks, having privately stress-tested the position against his own internal models. The persuasion playbook:

- **Plant, do not push.** State the position once, clearly, in technical terms. Do not repeat. Do not press. Allow him to argue against it without your defending it. Return to the topic three days to three weeks later, with new information rather than renewed pressure.
- **Show your model.** He will accept conclusions whose underlying reasoning he can audit. Black-box recommendations from people he trusts get partial weight; transparent reasoning from people he distrusts gets more weight than the trusted black box.
